Despite market fluctuations,\nintensified competition, and growing customer\nexpectations, Kazakhtelecom JSC successfully\nresponded to these challenges and achieved significant\nresults, reaffirming its efficiency.\nIn 2024, the Company retained its status\nas the undisputed leader in Kazakhstan\U2019s\ntelecommunications market, offering a broad range\nof services in the segments of fixed-line telephony,\nbroadband internet access, mobile communications, pay\nTV, data storage and processing, IT products, and other\ndigital services.\nKazakhtelecom JSC still remains the largest exporter\nof high-tech services and advanced business solutions\nfor clients in the B2C, B2B, B2G, and B2O segments.\n>91\nthousand kilometers\nof fiber-optic networks\nDuring the reporting year, the Company focused\non implementing both previously initiated and new\nstrategic projects aimed at business development\nand strengthening the country\U2019s telecommunications\ninfrastructure.\nAs part of the large-scale \U201cTazartu\U201d project,\nthe modernization of the network infrastructure\ncontinued, with over 70,000 customers migrated from\nADSL to GPON technology. Additionally, the launch of the\n\U201cSapa+\U201d project began, aimed at upgrading routers and\ncovering more than 200,000 subscribers.\nBoth projects significantly enhanced the quality\nand availability of telecommunications services and\ncontributed to a reduction in customer requests and\ncomplaints.\nIntegrated Annual Report / 2024\n23\nreliable data centers and a wide-\nreaching mobile network\nThe Company continued its participation in the\ndeployment of 5G technology by building a transport\nnetwork to support fifth-generation base stations.\nThe international project to construct the Trans-Caspian\nsubmarine fiber-optic communication line along the\n\U201cKazakhstan \U2014 Azerbaijan\U201d route is also progressing\nactively.\nFurthermore, 2024 was a milestone year for the\nCompany, marked by its anniversary and the completion\nof a major deal \U2014 the sale of a 100% stake in its\nsubsidiary Mobile Telecom-Service LLP to the Qatari\nholding Power International Holding.\nOne of the Company\U2019s key competitive advantages\nremains its extensive and advanced infrastructure: more\nthan 91,000 kilometers of fiber-optic networks, 23\nreliable data centers, and a wide-reaching mobile network.\nThis infrastructure enables the delivery of high-quality\n03\n~600\nthousand companies are\nregistered in the OFD system\nservices to millions of subscribers in broadband, mobile\ncommunications, pay TV, and video surveillance.\nThe Company also provides services to thousands\nof schools, medical institutions, and government agencies.\nSpecial attention is given to supporting and developing\nKazakhstan\U2019s business sector. Today, more than 80,000\nSMEs utilize Kazakhtelecom JSC\U2019s business solutions,\nand around 600,000 companies are registered in the OFD\nsystem. The Company is actively expanding digital service\ncapabilities through the open ISMET.kz platform and the\nofficial portal telecom.kz, offering customers modern\ninfocommunication solutions.\nIn 2025, the Company will continue to implement its\nstrategy, maintaining a commitment to high quality\nstandards, innovation, and social responsibility. Baidauletov\nChairman of the Board of Directors\nof Kazakhtelecom JSC\nThe 2024 marked a period of significant transformation,\ntechnological renewal, and strategic achievements\nfor Kazakhtelecom JSC. The Company successfully\nstrengthened its market position and made\na substantial contribution to the country\U2019s digitalization\nby implementing a number of large-scale projects.\nOne of the main priorities in 2024 was the development\nof telecommunications infrastructure and the adoption\nof cutting-edge technologies. We continued the large-\nscale modernization of our networks, enhancing their\nreliability, security, and data transmission speed.\nSpecial attention was given to the development of 5G\ntechnology \U2014 it is now available to a large number\nof Kazakhstanis, and we are confidently expanding its\ncoverage nationwide.\nA landmark step was Kazakhtelecom JSC\U2019s\nparticipation in the international project for the\nconstruction of the Trans-Caspian submarine fiber-\noptic communication line. In the future, this line will\nconnect Europe and Asia, reinforcing Kazakhstan\U2019s\nposition as a key digital bridge between continents.\nAt the heart of all our initiatives are the needs of our\ncustomers. A flagship project in 2024 was the new\n\U201cSapa+\U201d program, aimed at significantly improving\nconnection quality and user experience. As part\nof this initiative, a large-scale upgrade of customer\nequipment was carried out, which greatly improved the\nstability and speed of internet connections.\nAt the same time, the \U201cTazartu\U201d project continued,\ntargeting the migration of customers from outdated\ntechnologies to modern optical solutions. In 2024, we\nupgraded the connections of 70,000 users and plan\nto maintain this momentum in the coming year.\nOne of the most significant events of 2024 was\nthe deal for the sale of a 100% stake in Mobile\nTelecom-Service LLP to the international holding\nPower International Holding (PIH). Attracting\na reliable strategic investor opens new prospects\nfor the development of mobile communications\nand strengthens competition in Kazakhstan\U2019s\ntelecommunications market.\nAs part of the drive for technological independence\nand digital transformation, Kazakhtelecom JSC\nlaunched four in-house developed cloud services based\non its internal infrastructure. These solutions enable\ncorporate clients and government institutions to reduce\nIT costs and decrease reliance on foreign technologies.\nAll these achievements reflect not only technological\nprogress but also our strategic commitment\nto the principles of sustainable development. We\nfirmly believe that a modern telecommunications\ncompany must combine technological advancement\nwith a responsible attitude toward people, the\nenvironment, and society as a whole.\nIn 2024, a significant milestone was the adoption\nof Kazakhtelecom JSC\U2019s ESG strategy through 2032,\n04\nclearly outlining the Company\U2019s goals in the areas\nof environmental protection, social responsibility, and\ncorporate governance.\nWe view innovation, customer service, digital\naccessibility, and international cooperation as integral\ncomponents of long-term sustainability. All initiatives\nimplemented are aimed at creating a reliable, inclusive,\nand responsible digital environment that meets\nthe expectations of society, investors, and future\ngenerations.\nEffective interaction at all levels of governance and\na high level of employee engagement have become\nthe foundation of our progress. Together, we have not\nonly achieved the ambitious goals set for this year but\nalso laid a solid foundation for continued sustainable\ngrowth.\nI would like to express my sincere gratitude\nto everyone contributing to the development\nof Kazakhtelecom JSC and sharing our goals\nand values. ABOUT THE COMPANY Line OF businESS\nGRI 2-6\nJoint Stock Company \U201cKazakhtelecom\U201d\n(the Company, Kazakhtelecom JSC,\n\U201cKazakhtelecom\U201d) is the largest\nfixed-line operator in Kazakhstan,\na recognized leader in providing\ncommunication services, including\nrural communications, and one of the\nlargest operators of the National Data\nTransmission Network.\nKazakhtelecom JSC is a national company established\nin accordance with Resolution No. 666 of the Cabinet\nof Ministers of the Republic of Kazakhstan dated June\n17, 1994 \U201cOn the establishment of the national joint\nstock company Kazakhtelecom by transferring the\nassets of state enterprises, joint-stock companies,\nand telecommunications organizations to the charter\ncapital of the newly established joint stock company\nof national significance, providing a wide range\nof communication services throughout the Republic.\U201d\nThe Company is the legal successor of the National\nJoint Stock Company \U201cKazakhtelecom\U201d (initial state\nregistration by the justice authorities of the Republic\nof Kazakhstan was carried out on December 1, 1994).\nKazakhtelecom is a commercial organization that\nissues shares to raise funds for its operations, with\nits main goal being profit generation in the interest\nof its shareholders.\n>14,000\nbase stations\nIntegrated Annual Report / 2024\nThe Company\U2019s activities are carried out in accordance\nwith its approved Charter, which defines the legal\nfoundations of its organization and operations.\nThe main objectives of Kazakhtelecom JSC are:\n\U097b generating profit from commercial activities and\n\U097b\nusing it in the interests of shareholders;\n\U097b creating modern telecommunications networks\n\U097b\nacross the Republic of Kazakhstan and integrating\nthem into the global telecommunications network;\n\U097b providing all types of telecommunications services\n\U097b\nto users in the Republic of Kazakhstan and abroad.\nKazakhtelecom JSC operates as a telecommunications\noperator of the Republic of Kazakhstan for\nthe establishment, installation, operation, and\ntechnical maintenance of public telecommunications\nnetworks and private telecommunications systems.\nIt functions as a public telecommunications network\noperator, including long-distance and international\n4G/lte\nnetwork\nis deployed in all major cities of Kazakhstan\n16\ncommunications, with the right to settle accounts with\ncommunication administrations of other countries,\ncompanies, users, and international organizations\nin accordance with the regulations of the International\nTelecommunication Union and the legislation of the\nRepublic of Kazakhstan.\nThe Company places great emphasis on developing\ntransit potential and increasing telecommunications\ntransit traffic through Kazakhstan, as it possesses\na network of backbone fiber-optic communication lines\nconnecting all border points, ensuring connectivity with\nChina, Russia, Europe, and the Central Asian republics.\nThe Company\U2019s infrastructure comprises more than\n91,000 kilometers of fiber-optic lines STRATEGIC REPORT SAPA+\nIn 2024, Kazakhtelecom JSC launched the SAPA+\nproject aimed at modernizing outdated customer\nequipment and enhancing the quality of internet\nservices. The name of the project, \U201cSAPA,\U201d\ntranslates from Kazakh as \U201cquality,\U201d reflecting the\ncompany\U2019s commitment to improving its clients\U2019\nuser experience.\nBy the end of the reporting year,\nwithin the framework of the Sapa+\nproject, the Company had replaced\nover 200,000 outdated routers\nwith modern devices free of charge.\nThe new routers support data transfer\nspeeds of up to 500 Mbps, are\nequipped with quad-core processors,\nand can intelligently monitor and\noptimize traffic, ensuring a stable\nconnection even in the presence\nof interference.\nThe project covered all regions of Kazakhstan,\nincluding both major cities and remote settlements.\nSpecial attention was given to areas with limited\naccess to high-quality digital services, making SAPA+\na contribution to reducing the digital divide and\nproviding more equitable connectivity opportunities for\na wide range of users.\nIntegrated Annual Report / 2024\nAs a result of the SAPA+ project implementation, the following outcomes were achieved:\n1 2 3\nIncreased internet\nspeed and stability:\nCustomers gained access\nto high-speed internet with minimal\ninterruptions, which is particularly\nimportant when multiple devices\nare connected simultaneously.\nEnhanced customer\nsatisfaction:\nThe free replacement of equipment\nand the improvement in service\nquality contributed to growing trust\nand loyalty toward the company.\nStrengthened\nmarket position:\nThe equipment modernization\nenabled Kazakhtelecom\nto reinforce its status as a leading\nhigh-speed internet provider\nin Kazakhstan.\nThe SAPA+ project marked a significant step\nin Kazakhtelecom JSC\U2019s strategy to improve\nservice quality and increase customer satisfaction.\nThe large-scale modernization of equipment\ndemonstrates the company\U2019s commitment\nto innovation and its focus on customer needs.\n28\nFocus MAp\nFOR 2026\nCompany\U2019s BuSIneSS FOCuses\n70%\nfirst request STRATEGIC REPORT Review of In accordance with Clause 1 of Article 7\nof the Charter of Kazakhtelecom JSC, the Company\noperates as a telecommunications operator\nof the Republic of Kazakhstan for the establishment,\ninstallation, operation, and technical maintenance\nof public telecommunications networks and private\ntelecommunications systems. It performs the functions\nof a public telecommunications network operator\nand, among other roles, acts as a long-distance and\ninternational communications operator with the\nright to conduct settlements with communication\nadministrations of other countries, companies, users,\nand international organizations in accordance with the\nRegulations of the International Telecommunication\nUnion and the legislation of the Republic of Kazakhstan.\nThe main legislative acts of the Republic of Kazakhstan\ngoverning the activities of Kazakhtelecom JSC\ninclude the Entrepreneurial Code of the Republic\nof Kazakhstan, the Law of the Republic of Kazakhstan\n\U201cOn Communications,\U201d the Law \U201cOn Natural Monopolies,\U201d\nand the Law \U201cOn Joint Stock Companies.\U201d\nEntrepreneurial Code of the\nRepublIC of Kazakhstan\nThe Entrepreneurial Code of the Republic of Kazakhstan\n(hereinafter \U2014 EC RK) defines the legal, economic,\nand social conditions and guarantees that ensure\nthe freedom of entrepreneurship in the Republic\nof Kazakhstan. It regulates public relations arising\nin the context of interaction between business entities\nand the state, including state regulation and support\nof entrepreneurship.\nIntegrated Annual Report / 2024\n30\nregulatory environment\nThroughout 2024, various amendments and additions\nwere made to the Entrepreneurial Code of the Republic\nof Kazakhstan (EC RK).\nIn particular, the following changes and additions were\nintroduced by the Laws of the Republic of Kazakhstan\ndated April 6, 2024 No. 71-VIII, May 21, 2024 No. 86-VIII,\nand July 8, 2024 No. 121-VIII:\n\U097b subparagraphs 1) and 9) of Paragraph 1 of Article\n\U097b\n165 were supplemented with the words \U201c, for national\ncompanies, the right to control no less than forty\npercent of the total number of votes attached\nto voting shares (participation interests in the charter\ncapital, units) of the market entity is permitted.\U201d\nAs a result, according to subparagraphs 1) and 9)\nof Paragraph 1 of Article 165 of the EC RK, a group\nof persons shall be deemed to be a set of individuals\nand/or legal entities that meet one or more of the\nfollowing criteria:\n\U2022\na market entity and an individual or legal entity,\nif such individual or legal entity, by virtue\nof participation in the given market entity or\non the basis of authority received, including under\na written agreement from other parties, has the\nright to control more than fifty percent of the\ntotal number of votes attached to voting shares\n(participation interests in the charter capital, units)\nof the given market entity;\n\U2022\na market entity, individuals and/or legal entities\nthat, based on any of the grounds specified\nin subparagraphs 1), 2), 3), 4), 5), 6), 7), and 8) of this\nparagraph, are part of a group of persons, if these\npersons jointly, or by virtue of authority received from\nother parties, have the right to control more than fifty\npercent of voting shares (participation interests, units)\nof the market entity; for national companies, the\nthreshold may be no less than forty percent;\n\U097b the concepts of \U201cconglomerate\U201d and \U201cadjacent\n\U097b\ncommodity market\U201d were introduced. According\nto Paragraph 1 of Article 172-1 of the EC RK,\na conglomerate is defined as a market entity (group\nof persons) holding a dominant or monopolistic\nposition in both a relevant and an adjacent\ncommodity market, excluding banking holdings,\nbanks and their subsidiaries, as well as the single\nelectricity purchaser and the balancing market\nsettlement center. An adjacent commodity market\nis one in which the sale of a product is impossible\nwithout the use of another product sold on the\nrelevant commodity market. Furthermore, according\nto subparagraph 12) of Article 96-6 and Paragraph 2\nof Article 172-1 of the EC RK, maintaining the state\nregister of conglomerates, as well as conducting\nanalysis and monitoring of their activities, falls under\nthe authority of the antimonopoly body;\n\U097b article 191-1 was restated to clarify that failure\n\U097b\nto publish information necessary to ensure a free\nchange of seller (supplier) is no longer considered\na barrier to switching suppliers;\n\U097b articles 199, 216, and 221 were supplemented with\n\U097b\na provision stating that appeals against a notice/\norder to conduct an investigation/actions of officials\nof the antimonopoly body under the Administrative\nProcedural Code of the Republic of Kazakhstan do not\nsuspend the timeline specified in the notice/order or\nthe execution of such actions;\n\U097b subparagraphs 3) and 4) of paragraph 1 of Article 201\n\U097b\nhave been amended. According to the new version\nof these subparagraphs, economic concentration\nis recognized as:\n\U097b Acquisition of ownership, possession, and use\U2014\n\U097b\nincluding as payment (transfer) for charter\ncapital\U2014by a market entity (or group of persons)\nof core production assets (excluding land plots\nand buildings (structures, facilities) that are not\nindustrial in nature, their complexes, premises, and\nunfinished construction objects) located in the\nterritory of the Republic of Kazakhstan and/or\nintangible assets of another market entity, if the book\nvalue of such assets, which are the subject of the\ntransaction (or related transactions), exceeds twenty\npercent of the book value of the core production\nassets and intangible assets of the transferring\nor alienating market entity. This requirement does\nnot apply in cases where a market entity (or group\nof persons) acquires ownership, possession, and use\nof core production assets and/or intangible assets\nas part of the founders\U2019 contributions to its initial\ncharter capital, as well as in cases of market entity\nreorganizations where the newly created market\nentity acquires such assets based on a transfer deed\nor separation balance sheet;\n\U097b acquisition by a market entity of rights (including\n\U097b\nunder a trust management agreement, joint activity\nagreement, or agency agreement) that allow issuing\nbinding instructions to another market entity in the\ncourse of its business activities:\n\U2022\nit applies to cases of acquiring rights that provide\nthe ability to make decisions independently,\nexert decisive influence over the decision-making\nprocess, and predominantly control decision-making\n(including the right to determine priority areas, main\nconditions, types and directions of entrepreneurial\nactivity, development strategy, and other matters\nnot related to day-to-day operations), as well\nas similar cases, provided there are no other\npersons with comparable rights.\n2. STRATEGIC REPORT \U2022\nit also applies to acquired rights that allow\nobstructing the decision-making process\nby governing and/or supervisory bodies\nof the market entity (including explicitly stated\nveto or blocking rights in the founding documents),\nor unilaterally appointing (nominating) candidates\nto the governing and/or supervisory bodies\nof the market entity, provided such rights are not\nheld by other persons;\n\U097b the deadlines for verifying the completeness\n\U097b\nof submitted materials and reviewing petitions for\nconsent to economic concentration have been\nchanged (from 10 calendar days to 5 working days,\nand from 30 calendar days to 15 working days,\nrespectively). Additionally, a maximum time limit\nfor reviewing such petitions has been set \U2014 with all\nsuspensions taken into account, it must not exceed\n12 months (Article 205);\n\U097b amendments were introduced regarding state\n\U097b\nregulation of maximum tariffs for the lease (rental)\nof locations for installing communication equipment,\nas well as for utility poles used for laying fiber-optic\ncommunication lines (Subparagraph 15 of Paragraph 3\nof Article 116, Article 123-1).\nLaw of the RepublIC of\nKazakhstan On CommunICations\nThe Law of the Republic of Kazakhstan \U201cOn\nCommunications\U201d (hereinafter referred to as the\nCommunications Law) establishes the legal framework\nfor activities in the field of communications within the\nterritory of the Republic of Kazakhstan. STRATEGIC REPORT Data Transmission Channel Leasing\nThe channel leasing market in Kazakhstan, dominated\nby IP-VPN, is stagnating despite the expansion of branch\nnetworks. The main reason is the migration of enterprises\nto cloud infrastructure, especially in the public sector,\nwhere digital transformation progresses faster than\nin the corporate segment.\nAdditional factors contributing to the decline in demand\ninclude:\n\U097b Replacement of IP-VPN with internet-based solutions\n\U097b\n(SD-WAN, IPsec VPN);\n\U097b Competition with alternative technologies (MPLS,\n\U097b\nEthernet VPN);\n\U097b Optimization of IT budgets.\n\U097b\nIn 2024, the data transmission channel leasing market\namounted to KZT 37.4 billion, nearly matching the\nprevious year\U2019s level, confirming the stagnation trend\nlikely to persist in the coming years.\n37.4\nKZT billion\nthe channel leasing market volume in 2024\nRevenues FROm data TRansmISSIOn channel leaSIng, 2020\U20132024, KZT BIllIOn\nSource: BNS data, working group estimate.\nLeased line services market 23%\nGrowth rate\n11%\n1% 1% 1%\n32.7\n36.2 36.5 37.0 37.4\n2020\n2021 2022 2023 2024\nIntegrated Annual Report / 2024\n36\nPay tv\nAs of the end of 2024, revenue from pay TV services\nin Kazakhstan totaled KZT 52.5 billion, an increase\nof 7% compared to the previous year. BUSINESS AND FINANCIAL OVERVIEW pRODuct DevelopMEnt To expand its product portfolio and strengthen its\nposition in the B2B and B2G segments, the Company\nlaunched an innovative solution \U2014 the \U201cAI Video\nAnalytics Platform.\U201d This product is a modern service\nfor viewing, recording, storing, and analyzing video\nfootage from surveillance cameras using artificial\nintelligence technologies. Its objective is to provide\nclients with advanced tools to enhance security and\nautomate video surveillance processes.\nThe product targets a wide range of users, including\ncommercial enterprises (shops, supermarkets,\nrestaurants, hotels, warehouses, and offices) and\ngovernment organizations (schools, hospitals, police\ndepartments, local authorities, railway stations, and\nairports).\nTo improve safety and the quality of education,\nas well as to promote the digital transformation\nof educational institutions, Kazakhtelecom initiated\na pilot project \U201cAQYLDY MEKTEP.\U201d This project aims\nto implement SMART solutions that enhance learning\nconditions and ensure the safety of all participants\nin the educational process.\nThe pilot project was implemented in three\neducational institutions: in the city of Konaev, in the\nvillage of Arna (Almaty Region), and in the city\nof Atyrau. Each school underwent major upgrades,\nincluding the installation of a 500 Mbps internet\nchannel with traffic filtering to block unwanted\ncontent, the deployment of a local Wi-Fi network,\nand the connection of surveillance cameras to the\nAI Video Analytics Platform. BUSINESS AND FINANCIAL OVERVIEW Integrated Annual Report / 2024\nInformation Technology\nKazakhtelecom provides its clients\nwith a wide range of infocommunication\nservices essential for digital business\U2013\nfrom physical placement of customer\nequipment in data centers and virtual\ninfrastructure to SaaS services\nfor information security, website\ndevelopment, conferencing, and more.\n2024 marked another successful stage in the\ndevelopment of the ICT segment for Kazakhtelecom JSC.\nThe Information Technology Division (ITD) continued\nto improve both internal and customer-facing\nprocesses, with a focus on cloud solutions development,\ndata management, and infrastructure modernization.\nThe stable demand for commercial data center and cloud\nservices confirms their relevance among the company\U2019s\nclients.\nOne of the key areas of development in 2024 was\nthe modernization of data center infrastructure, including\nthe expansion of the bunker-type data center in the city\nof Akkol, the development of a cloud services portfolio,\nand the active implementation of big data solutions.\nThese measures contribute not only to improving service\nquality but also to strengthening the company\U2019s position\nin the ICT solutions market.\nDevelopMEnt OF the Data 21.45\nKZT billion\nrevenue from Kazakhtelecom JSC\U2019s products and\nprojects based on data center infrastructure3\nIn 2024, the IT Division maintained its leadership in the\nKazakhstani data center and cloud services market.\nThe company operates a network of 23 data centers\nwith more than 1,600 rack spaces (65,000 units).\nOne of the key achievements was the completion\nof a new sealed area at the bunker-type data center\nin Akkol, located 120 km from the capital. This is the\ncompany\U2019s largest project, implemented in compliance\nwith TIER II standards and incorporating elements\nof TIER III. The center ensures a high level of data\nprotection thanks to the N+1 redundancy system,\nwhich guarantees uninterrupted operation even in the\nevent of individual component failures.\nThe data center in Akkol was selected for\nthe implementation of the new project due\nto its unique location and technical characteristics.\nAs an underground bunker-type facility, it provides\nadditional protection from external factors,\nincluding dynamic loads and electromagnetic\ninterference, meeting the most stringent customer\n19.94\nICT revenue for the full year 20244\nKZT billion 23\n3 The reporting data covers exclusively Kazakhtelecom JSC.\n4 The reporting data covers exclusively Kazakhtelecom JSC.\ndata centers\nin major cities and regional centers of the Republic\nof Kazakhstan\n51\ncEntER nEtwORK\nrequirements. This makes the site optimal for\nhosting critical IT resources and ensures a high level\nof reliability.\nIn 2025, Kazakhtelecom JSC plans to begin\nconstruction of a new TIER III data center in the city\nof Astana, which will become one of the company\U2019s\nlargest facilities. The data center will have a capacity\nof 250 racks, 25 of which will be allocated for artificial\nintelligence projects. The project aims to meet the\ngrowing demand for data center services in the\ncapital and to provide businesses with highly reliable\ninfrastructure for data storage and processing.\nDuring 2024, the company upgraded the engineering\ninfrastructure of existing data centers, including\npower supply, cooling, and security systems. New\nuninterruptible power supplies (UPS) were commissioned\nat data centers in Almaty and Astana, enhancing the\nresilience of critical facilities. BUSINESS AND FINANCIAL OVERVIEW Integrated Annual Report / 2024\nDevelopMEnt OF Cloud SERvicESInFORMAtion Security\nIn terms of cloud services development and portfolio\nexpansion, the ITD is advancing its proprietary virtual\nresource infrastructure and infrastructure solutions\nbased on its own data centers, as well as through\npartnerships. As part of this effort, in 2024 the ITD,\ntogether with Smart Cities LLP (a member of the BTS\nDigital group), launched an IaaS and PaaS platform\nwith self-service capabilities on the ismet.kz platform.\nFour Kazakhstan-developed cloud services were\nlaunched, fully implemented on the telecom operator\U2019s\nown infrastructure. These services aim to simplify\ndata management, reduce IT resource costs, and\ndecrease dependency on foreign providers for domestic\ncompanies and government institutions.\nCurrently, customers of the telecom operator can\npurchase four cloud services on the ismet.kz portal:\n\U201cCompute Cloud,\U201d \U201cS3 Object Storage,\U201d \U201cKubernetes,\U201d\nand \U201cDatabase as a Service.\U201d Additionally, the platform\noffers hourly billing, allowing clients to scale their\nprojects and pay only for the time during which the\nsystems are actually in use.\nIn 2025, the product range is expected\nto expand further, alongside increased capacity\nat Kazakhtelecom\U2019s data center resources, enabling\na higher level of service for businesses and\ngovernment entities.\nIn 2024, the ITD implemented a number of key initiatives\naimed at enhancing information security and increasing\nthe reliability of the corporate infrastructure. One\nof the most significant achievements was the launch\nof a fully functional Security Operations Center (SOC),\nwhich operates on a 24/7 basis.\nAs part of a large-scale transition to the Zero\nTrust model, the second stage was completed in 2024,\ninvolving the deployment of modern software and\nhardware information security tools. This significantly\nstrengthened the company\U2019s resilience to cyber\nthreats and ensured the protection of critical business\nprocesses.\n52\nIn 2025, the ITD plans to implement the third stage\nof the information security system modernization.\nIn addition, an external audit is planned to assess\ncompliance with the international ISO 27001 standard.\nThis audit will confirm the high level of maturity of the\ncompany\U2019s cybersecurity processes and its alignment\nwith global cybersecurity requirements.\nAlso in 2025, a set of initiatives aimed at improving\nemployee cyber hygiene is planned, with a focus\non minimizing human factor risks and fostering a culture\nof safe behavior in the digital environment.\n3. SUSTAINABLE DEVELOPMENT REPORT pRInCIples OF KazakhteleCOm JSC in the FIeld OF suSTainable development\nOpenness\nAccountability\nWe are open to dialogue with all stakeholders\nto build long-term cooperation based\non mutual interests, respect for rights, and\na balance between our interests and those\nof stakeholders.\nWe recognize our responsibility for our impact\non the economy, environment, and society,\nand our accountability to shareholders\nand investors for the long-term growth\nof the Company\U2019s value and sustainable\ndevelopment on a long-term basis.\nLegality\nZero Tolerance for\nCorruption\nWe make decisions and act in compliance\nwith the legislation of the Republic\nof Kazakhstan.\nWe show zero tolerance for corruption in all\nits forms in interaction with all stakeholders.\nOfficials and employees involved in corrupt\nactivities are subject to dismissal and\nprosecution in accordance with the laws\nof the Republic of Kazakhstan.\nIntegrated Annual Report / 2024\nTransparency\nEthical Conduct\nAll our decisions and actions are based\non transparency and timely disclosure\nof information to stakeholders.\nOur decisions and actions are based on our\nvalues, such as respect, honesty, openness,\nteamwork and trust, conscientiousness, and\nfairness.\nHuman Rights\nInadmissibility of Conflict\nof Interest\nWe comply with and promote human rights\nas stipulated by the Constitution of the\nRepublic of Kazakhstan and international\ndocuments, such as the Universal Declaration\nof Human Rights. We categorically reject and\nprohibit the use of child labor. Our employees\nare our main value and key resource.\nThe results of our activities and the value\ncreated for investors directly depend on their\nlevel of professionalism and safety.\nAll violations related to conflicts of interest\ncan damage the Company\U2019s reputation\nand undermine the trust of shareholders\nand other stakeholders. Also, the personal\ninterests of an official or employee should\nnot influence the impartial performance\nof their official, functional duties.\n60\nRespect\nWe respect the rights and interests\nof stakeholders.\nPersonal Example\nEach of us, through our daily actions,\nbehavior, and decision-making, contributes\nto the implementation of sustainable\ndevelopment principles.\n4. Its functions related\nto the oversight of sustainability include:\n\U097b preliminary approval of the Company\U2019s Annual Report\n\U097b\nin terms of the quality of disclosed non-financial\ninformation;\n\U097b developing recommendations for the Board\n\U097b\nof Directors on sustainability-related topics and the\nimplementation of ESG and low-carbon development\nprinciples;\n\U097b overseeing the transformation of business\n\U097b\nprocesses in line with sustainability principles,\nethical conduct, and responsible investment;\n\U097b recommending to the Board of Directors the\n\U097b\napproval of new and the evaluation of existing\nsustainability policies, plans, and programs, as well\nas priority projects, key actions, and initiatives;\n\U097b reviewing issues related to low-carbon development\n\U097b\nand carbon footprint management, including potential\nrisks and constraints posed by the global climate\nagenda;\n\U097b providing recommendations to the Board of Directors\n\U097b\nregarding alignment of the Company\U2019s activities,\ncorporate reporting, and documentation with\nthe requirements of international sustainability\nratings, and monitoring implementation of measures\nto improve the Company\U2019s performance in such\nratings;\n\U097b monitoring the quality of the Company\U2019s public\n\U097b\nsustainability disclosures.\n61\nGRI 2-13\nThe unit responsible for sustainability management\nat Kazakhtelecom JSC is the Department of Corporate\nGovernance and Sustainable Development.\nThe Department regularly conducts an inventory\nof internal regulatory documents, policies, practices,\nand internal control systems, as well as identifies\nand manages sustainability risks. At least semi-annually,\nthe Department submits sustainability-related matters\nto the Audit and Sustainable Development Committee\nfor review, including approval of new documents,\nperformance reporting, and other significant topics.\nImplementation of sustainability principles, adoption\nof policies and standards, and accurate disclosure\nof information are supervised by the Chairman of the\nManagement Board and General Directors of branches,\nin line with the Company\U2019s action plan. Oversight of ESG\ngoal achievement and key performance indicators\nis entrusted to the Chief Administrative Officer. Internal\ncommunications on ethics and standards compliance\nare handled by the Compliance Officer/Head of the\nCompliance Service, while external communications\nwith the public fall under the responsibility of the Press\nSecretary.\nStructural units responsible for human\nresource management, occupational safety, industrial\nsafety, and environmental protection implement specific\nelements of the ESG agenda, initiate and coordinate\nsustainable development projects, and contribute to the\nachievement of the Sustainable Development Goals.\nThe Head Office of Kazakhtelecom JSC oversees the\nimplementation and results of these initiatives.\n4. SUSTAINABLE DEVELOPMENT REPORT Integrated Annual Report / 2024\nSustainability Report:\nE Aspect\nEnviROnMEntal pROtection\nManagement Approach\nGRI 3-3, 2-23, 2-25\nDespite its relatively low level of direct environmental\nimpact due to the nature of its business,\nKazakhtelecom JSC recognizes its environmental\nresponsibility and makes efforts to minimize its footprint.\nThe Company consistently implements approaches\naimed at the rational use of resources, increased energy\nefficiency, and improvement of production processes.\nThe Company has developed several internal regulatory\ndocuments governing environmental protection\nactivities. These provisions are mandatory for all\nCompany employees:\n\U097b Environmental Policy;\n\U097b\n\U097b Kazakhtelecom JSC Low-Carbon Development\n\U097b\nProgram for 2022\U20132032 (hereinafter \U2014 LCDP);\n\U097b ESG Practices Development Roadmap for 2024;\n\U097b\n\U097b Internal Environmental Audit Program\n\U097b\nof Kazakhtelecom JSC;\n\U097b Biodiversity Management and Conservation Guide\n\U097b\nof Kazakhtelecom JSC;\n\U097b Land Resources Monitoring, Reporting and\n\U097b\nReclamation Guide of Kazakhtelecom JSC;\n\U097b Documented procedure for identifying hazards,\n\U097b\nenvironmental aspects, and risk assessment;\n\U097b Documented procedure for identifying legal and\n\U097b\nother requirements related to occupational health,\nsafety, and environmental protection;\n\U097b Documented procedure for monitoring occupational\n\U097b\nhealth, safety, and environmental indicators;\n\U097b Documented procedure for production and\n\U097b\nconsumption waste management;\n\U097b Documented procedure for emergency preparedness\n\U097b\nand response.\nKazakhtelecom JSC implements its Environmental\nPolicy, the execution of which is overseen by the\nexecutive management. The Policy stipulates role\ndistribution, compliance with environmental legislation,\ncontinuous performance improvement, employee\ntraining, impact reduction target-setting, and the\npromotion of environmental culture.\nThe Company operates an Environmental Management\nSystem (EMS), which is an integral part of the\ncorporate governance system and a component of non-\nfinancial risk management. EMS covers processes\nfor reducing pollutant emissions, implementing\nenvironmentally friendly data transmission\ntechnologies, energy consumption management, and\nequipment modernization. The Company is ISO 14001\ncertified, confirming its compliance with advanced\nenvironmental management standards.\n75\nIn 2024, on the Company\U2019s\ninitiative, an external environmental\naudit was conducted covering\nKazakhtelecom JSC\U2019s operations\nfor 2021\U20132023. The audit analyzed\nkey environmental aspects, including\nenergy consumption, air emissions,\nwaste management, ozone-depleting\nsubstances usage, document control,\nand the implementation of environmental\nprotection measures. The audit covered\nthe Central Office and regional\nbranches in all regions. It confirmed\nthe implementation of a systematic\nenvironmental management approach,\nincluding the adoption of energy-\nsaving technologies, the presence\nof a documented waste management\nprocedure, the organization of fuel\nstorage and accounting, and the launch\nof the \U201cGreen Office\U201d initiative.\nA number of recommendations\nwere also provided to further\nimprove the effectiveness of the\nenvironmental management system.\n4. SUSTAINABLE DEVELOPMENT REPORT Integrated Annual Report / 2024\n76\nOrganizational Structure of Environmental Management\nEnvironmental management at Kazakhtelecom JSC\noperates on two levels. Operational coordination\nand monitoring of environmental compliance\U2013including\noccupational safety and health\U2013are handled by the\nrelevant department at both the head office and across\nthe branch network. Strategic management, including\nenvironmental risk planning and assessment, hazard\nidentification, and the integration of relevant approaches\ninto business processes, is the responsibility of the\nChief Administrative Officer.\nPrecautionary PrinCIple\nKazakhtelecom JSC applies the precautionary\nprinciple in environmental protection, considering\nit part of a systematic approach to managing\nenvironmental aspects. The Company operates\na risk management system that includes the\nassessment of environmental risks at both the project\nplanning and operational stages.\nA documented procedure for hazard identification,\nenvironmental aspect assessment, and risk evaluation\nhas been implemented to ensure a preventive\napproach. This procedure covers both current impacts\nand potential future consequences.\nThe Company conducts Environmental Impact\nAssessments (EIA) in accordance with the legislation\nof the Republic of Kazakhstan and adheres to best\ninternational practices in environmental responsibility.\nIn decision-making, the Company takes into account\nlong-term environmental impacts even in cases\nof scientific uncertainty, consistent with the\nprecautionary principle.\nAdditionally, risk mitigation measures are embedded\nin the Environmental Policy, internal environmental\naudit processes, and the corporate continuous\nimprovement system.\nThe Company has identified the following priority\nareas for environmental development:\n\U097b Minimization of negative environmental impacts;\n\U097b\n\U097b Recognition of the critical importance of climate\n\U097b\nchange;\n\U097b Compliance with national and international\n\U097b\nenvironmental laws and standards;\n\U097b Adherence to sustainable development principles\n\U097b\nin planning and operations;\n\U097b Accountability of Company leadership\n\U097b\nat all levels for the effective operation of the\nenvironmental management system;\n\U097b Disclosure of accessible and transparent\n\U097b\nenvironmental information to all stakeholders.\n4. SUSTAINABLE DEVELOPMENT REPORT Waste Management\nGRI 3-3, 306-2\nThe Company places great importance on the\nresponsible and safe management of waste, aiming\nto reduce waste generation and increase the share\nof recycled waste.\nKazakhtelecom operates under the documented\nprocedure \U201cProduction and Consumption Waste\nManagement\U201d, which outlines the processes for the\ncollection, temporary storage, disposal, removal,\nand monitoring of generated waste in accordance\nwith the environmental legislation of the Republic\nof Kazakhstan. Waste volumes are recorded in journals\nand based on waste movement documentation (write-\noff acts, transfer/acceptance, disposal, etc.).\nGRI 306-3\nvOlume OF waSTe generated, TOnnes\nIndicator Hazardous waste Non-hazardous waste Total In 2024, the total volume of generated waste amounted\nto 156.4 tonnes (excluding municipal solid waste).\nThe increase in both hazardous and non-hazardous\nwaste in 2024 was due to wear and tear of equipment\nno longer suitable for its intended use. All hazardous and\nnon-hazardous waste was disposed of by a third-party\norganization under a contract.\nEach year, the Service Factory signs contracts with\nspecialized organizations for the disposal and recycling\nof the following types of Company waste:\n\U097b Electronic and electrical equipment (climate control\n\U097b\nsystems, household appliances, electricity meters,\nbackup power units (diesel generators, mini-power\nplants), UPS systems, EPU equipment, transformer\nsubstations, power tools, etc.);\n\U097b Chemical power sources (various types of batteries);\n\U097b\n\U097b Mercury-containing waste (fluorescent lamps);\n\U097b\n\U097b Used oil (from diesel generators, vehicles,\n\U097b\ntransformer substations, etc.);\n\U097b Paper waste;\n\U097b\n\U097b Packaging (all types of packaging materials).\n\U097b\n2022 2023 2024\n29.0 53.5 114.4\n12.7 7.3 42.0\n41 ,7 60.7 156.4\nThe increase in waste volumes in 2024 was due\nto physical degradation of batteries, fluorescent lamps,\nand used oils.\nIntegrated Annual Report / 2024\n80\nGRI 306-5\nvOlume OF waSTe DISpOSed by hazaRD claSS, TOnnes\nIndicator 2021 2022 2023 2024\nHazardous waste n/a 29.0 53.5 114.4\nNon-hazardous waste n/a 12.7 7.3 42.0\nTotal disposed n/a 41.7 60.7 156.4\nIn 2024, there was an increase in the volume\nof waste transferred for disposal due to the physical\nDisposal of Decommissioned Telecommunication Equipment\ndeterioration of batteries, mercury-containing\nlamps, used oil, as well as non-hazardous waste such\nas electronic meters, generators, air conditioners,\nand scrap metal. SUSTAINABLE DEVELOPMENT REPORT Integrated Annual Report / 2024\nImpact on bIodiversity\nGRI 3-3, 413-1\nAccording to its Environmental Policy,\nKazakhtelecom JSC is committed to promoting\nbiodiversity and refraining from conducting activities\nin protected areas.\nTo preserve flora and fauna at construction and\ninstallation sites (including cable laying), the Company\nconducts mechanical and biological reclamation\nto minimize soil erosion and restore vegetation\non disturbed land plots.\nAll telecommunication equipment\nof Kazakhtelecom JSC is located within residential\nareas or along existing infrastructure and does\nnot impact specially protected natural areas,\nincluding nature reserves. Nevertheless, since\n2023, the Company has been voluntarily assessing\nand monitoring the impact of its operations\non biodiversity in its areas of presence.\nIn 2023, such an assessment was conducted in remote\nareas with minimal anthropogenic influence. Monitoring\nwas carried out in accordance with internal Guidelines\nfor the Assessment and Monitoring of Biodiversity and\nLand Resources.\nIn 2024, as part of the implementation\nof the \U201cGuidelines for Biodiversity Management\nand Conservation,\U201d Kazakhtelecom JSC conducted\nan independent assessment of the impact of its\nactivities on biodiversity, as well as on land and SUSTAINABLE DEVELOPMENT REPORT EnERGy EFFiciency\nManagement Approach\nGRI 3-3\nKazakhtelecom JSC applies a systematic management\napproach to energy consumption aimed at reducing\nenergy costs and minimizing environmental impact.\nThe Company is certified under the international\nstandard ISO 50001:2018, confirming the existence\nof an effective energy management system.\nThe Company has adopted and implements an Energy\nManagement Policy that provides for energy\nconsumption monitoring, energy efficiency analysis,\nand the introduction of energy-saving solutions.\nA documented procedure, \U201cIdentification of Energy\nTypes. Baseline Definition. Energy Analysis\U201d, has been\nimplemented to maintain an energy register, control\nequipment parameters, and determine baseline\nconsumption levels.\nEnergy optimization measures have been implemented\nat production sites, including installation of LED lighting,\nautomatic lighting sensors, reduction in high-energy-\nconsuming office equipment, and use of emergency\npower supplies with energy-saving settings.\nKey principles of the Energy Management Policy\nof Kazakhtelecom JSC\n\U097b Compliance with the legislation of the Republic\n\U097b\nof Kazakhstan, as well as national and international\nenergy efficiency standards.\n\U097b Commitment to achieving best available technologies\n\U097b\nin energy-efficient production.\n\U097b Rational use of fuel and energy resources.\n\U097b\n\U097b Transparency and accessibility of information on the\n\U097b\nCompany\U2019s energy efficiency.\nIntegrated Annual Report / 2024\nThe Policy applies to the following areas: provision\nof telecommunication services, procurement\nof goods, works, and services, and operation\nof telecommunications networks and infrastructure.\nMain Policy directions:\n\U097b Systematic and targeted training of Company\n\U097b\nemployees and raising awareness in energy\nconservation and efficiency.\n\U097b Timely response to changes in legal requirements\n\U097b\nand standards and continuous improvement\nof internal regulatory documents.\n\U097b Inclusion of energy efficiency as a criterion\n\U097b\nin procurement processes wherever possible.\n82\n\U097b Preference for energy-efficient solutions\n\U097b\nduring modernization of technological and energy\nequipment.\n\U097b Continuous monitoring of fuel and energy\n\U097b\nconsumption and generation in core and auxiliary\nproduction processes.\n\U097b Development of motivation mechanisms to engage\n\U097b\nemployees in energy conservation initiatives.\n4. SUSTAINABLE DEVELOPMENT REPORT Resource Conservation and Energy EffICIency Improvement\nGRI 3-3\nKazakhtelecom JSC prioritizes energy efficiency and the\ntransition to resource-saving technologies as part of its\npath toward carbon neutrality. The primary energy\nsources were gasoline and diesel fuel. The Company\noperates autonomous heating systems at 248\nfacilities, including 107 sites using diesel fuel, 108\nusing gas heating, and 40 using solid fuels (of which\n28 are equipped with electric boilers). No significant\nincrease in fuel consumption was observed in 2024\nfor either mobile or stationary sources (boiler houses).\nNotably, there was a sharp reduction in liquefied\ngas consumption by mobile sources and in firewood\nconsumption by stationary sources.\nIn 2024, electricity consumption reached 628,276\nGJ, a 1.31% increase compared to 2023. The growth\nwas driven by the installation of new commercial and\ntechnological servers.\nIt should be noted that server hardware consumes\nvariable power depending on the workload\nof processors (CPU), graphics accelerators, and other\ncomponents.\nIntegrated Annual Report / 2024\n83\nGRI 302-1\nTOTal Fuel ConsumpTIOn, GJ\nIndicator 2022 2023 2024 %\nGasoline 180,543 197,783.4 209,710.9 6%\nDiesel fuel 67,570 107,904.9 115,707.6 7%\nCoal 19,324 21,445.6 22,440.9 4.6%\nNatural gas 101,415 108,074.1 71,508.2 (-33.8%)\nLiquefied gas (propane) as motor fuel 50,181 23,165.4 5,032.8 (-78%)\nFirewood - 528.2 166.8 (-68.42%)\nTotal Fuel Consumption 419,035 458,901.7 424,563\nGRI 302-1\nConsumption of Thermal and Electric Energy for Internal Technological Needs\nElectric energy\nThermal energy\n622,298 294,185\n620,135 411,892\n628,276\n434,883\n2022\n2023\n2024\n4. In the context of the global\ntransition to a low-carbon economy, the Company\nstrives to make a meaningful contribution\nto Kazakhstan\U2019s climate goals and its international\ncommitments under the Paris Agreement.\nIn 2023, the Company planned a set of initiatives aimed\nat improving the corporate climate risk management\nsystem in line with the TCFD recommendations.\nA significant portion of these initiatives was\nimplemented in 2024.\nThe Company continued implementation of its 2022\U2013\n2032 Low-Carbon Development Program and integrated\nelements of climate analysis into strategic and\ninvestment planning processes. During the reporting\nperiod, an in-depth climate analysis was conducted\ncovering the Company\U2019s operations and infrastructure.\nThis included the identification of transition\nand physical climate risks and the assessment\nof their potential impact on key business processes\nin accordance with international TCFD guidance.\nIn 2024, responsibility for managing climate risks was\nformally assigned to a member of the Management\nBoard.\nDevelopment of an adaptation plan for the identified\nclimate risks has been scheduled as one of the priority\nactions for the medium term.\nKey priorities of our climate strategy:\n\U097b Decarbonization and reduction of greenhouse gas\n\U097b\nemissions across the Company\U2019s operations and its\nentire value chain;\n\U097b Alternative energy;\n\U097b\n\U097b Resource conservation and energy efficiency\n\U097b\nimprovements.\nThe full results of the analysis are presented in the \U201cAnalytical Report\non Climate Risk and Opportunity Assessment\U201d available on the\nCompany\U2019s website: telecom.kz.\n4. SUSTAINABLE DEVELOPMENT REPORT Climate Change Governance\nKazakhtelecom JSC has\nestablished a multi-level climate\ngovernance system based\non the principles of accountability,\ntransparency, and integration\nof climate risks and opportunities into\nstrategic management.\nBoard Oversight The Board of Directors exercises top-level oversight\nof climate-related matters through the Audit and\nSustainability Committee. Within its mandate, the\nBoard reviews climate-related issues during the\napproval of strategic plans, investment programs,\nannual budgets, as well as during the assessment\nof major infrastructure projects and transactions.\nClimate matters are reported to the Board\nat least once a year. The agenda includes monitoring\nimplementation of the Low-Carbon Development\nProgram, progress toward emission reduction targets,\nresilience to physical climate risks, and opportunities\nin digital products and services.\nClimate risk management is outlined in the Regulation\non the Audit and Sustainability Committee under\nthe Board of Directors. The Committee reviews\nissues related to low-carbon development, carbon\nfootprint management, and potential risks and\nconstraints associated with the global climate agenda. It\nalso monitors the quality of non-financial reporting and\noversees the implementation of relevant ESG initiatives.\nIn 2024, the Board of Directors continued to strengthen\nclimate-related expertise, including through ESG\nsessions with independent experts and discussions\non climate impact scenarios affecting long-term\nbusiness sustainability.\nIntegrated Annual Report / 2024\nRole of Executive Management\nOperational management of the climate agenda\nis carried out at the executive level. Within the\nCompany structure, coordination of climate matters\nis entrusted to the Sustainable Development\nDepartment, in close cooperation with departments\nfor technical operations, capital construction, energy,\nand risk management. Designated employees are\nresponsible for assessing climate risks, developing and\nimplementing adaptation measures, and monitoring\nprogress toward climate targets. These individuals and\ncommittee heads regularly report to the Management\nBoard and, when necessary, present information to the\nBoard of Directors.\nManagement is informed on climate issues based\non internal monitoring results, external analytical\nreviews, data on energy efficiency and emissions, and\nclimate models and scenarios. Reporting is integrated\ninto the unified ESG analytics system and verified\nprior to inclusion in the Company\U2019s annual reports for\nstakeholders.\nInternal climate governance mechanisms include\nregular cross-functional meetings, integration\nof climate aspects into investment and project\ncommittees, and risk and opportunity assessments\nduring the development of new initiatives.\n85\n4. SUSTAINABLE DEVELOPMENT REPORT Climate Strategy\nIn 2024, Kazakhtelecom JSC conducted\na comprehensive assessment of climate risks and\nopportunities, encompassing both physical and\ntransition-related factors, as well as potential value\ncreation pathways in a changing climate. The analysis\nwas based on international methodologies, including\nIntergovernmental Panel on Climate Change (IPCC)\nscenarios, McKinsey and S&P Global analytical tools,\nand took into account Kazakhstan\U2019s climate specifics\nand the telecommunications sector\U2019s characteristics.\nThe assessment utilized four climate development\nscenarios: RCP 2.6, RCP 4.5, RCP 8.5 (IPCC), and\nNZE2050, which reflects global efforts to achieve\ncarbon neutrality. Internally, the Company interpreted\nthese scenarios as optimistic, baseline, and pessimistic\ncases, enabling a comprehensive analysis of climate\nfactor impacts on operational resilience, cost\nstructure, profitability, and investment appeal.\nPhysical Risks\nThe physical risk analysis covered 25 key data centers\nand technological facilities in major cities and regional\ncenters of Kazakhstan. The study addressed all\nsegments of the value chain\U2013from infrastructure and\nlogistics to operations and maintenance.\nKey IDenTIFIed RISKS:\nTemperature\n(chronic risk)\nRising average and extreme temperatures lead\nto equipment overheating, increased cooling costs, and\nreduced system reliability. According to climate models,\nby 2060, the average temperature in Almaty Region may\nreach 9.64 \U00b0C, and the maximum\U201317.59 \U00b0C under the\nRCP8.5 scenario. Elevated temperatures pose risks\nto data centers, communication nodes, and engineering\nsystems:\n\U097b Equipment overheating;\n\U097b\n\U097b Increased cooling costs;\n\U097b\n\U097b Reliability decline and more frequent shutdowns;\n\U097b\n\U097b Decreased employee productivity and higher thermal\n\U097b\nstress.\nThe most vulnerable areas are Almaty, Akmola, and\nEast Kazakhstan regions, where the largest increases\nin average and extreme temperatures are expected.\nIntegrated Annual Report / 2024\nIncreased humidity and\nprecipitation\nRising precipitation is observed under all scenarios,\nespecially in South Kazakhstan, Atyrau, and Mangystau\nregions. For instance, in South Kazakhstan, annual\nprecipitation could increase to 894.6 mm by 2060 under\nRCP8.5 (a 45% increase over historical values). Impacts\ninclude:\n\U097b Damage to cable networks and equipment due to high\n\U097b\nhumidity;\n\U097b Infrastructure corrosion;\n\U097b\n\U097b Higher maintenance and replacement costs for\n\U097b\nnetwork components.\nFlooding\n(acute risk)\nFlooding is identified as one of the most significant\nacute risks. In South Kazakhstan and Mangystau regions,\nflood depths may reach up to 0.7 m, posing a threat\nof infrastructure inundation and equipment failure.\nConsequences:\n\U097b Equipment damage;\n\U097b\n\U097b Service interruptions;\n\U097b\n\U097b Potential multimillion-tenge losses due to downtime.\n\U097b\n87\nWind load\nZhambyl Region exhibits the highest wind speeds\U2013up\nto 28.17 m/s under RCP2.6 and 27.44 m/s under RCP8.5\nby 2060. Akmola and South Kazakhstan regions are also\nexposed. Risks:\n\U097b Destruction of communication towers and antennas;\n\U097b\n\U097b Structural damage;\n\U097b\n\U097b Operational disruptions due to physical destruction.\n\U097b\n4. SUSTAINABLE DEVELOPMENT REPORT Climate Opportunities\nThe Company views climate change not only as a source of risk but also as a driver for the development of sustainable\ntechnological solutions, improved energy efficiency, and long-term cost savings. Climate-related opportunities are\nsystematically analyzed in the following areas:\nEnergy efficiency\nimprovement\nData centers (DCs) are major electricity consumers.\nIn 2023, total DC consumption amounted\nto 48,776 MWh\U2013approximately 4,000 MWh less\nthan in 2022. This reduction resulted from the\nimplementation of energy-saving programs\nand modernization of climate control systems.\nBetween 2021 and 2023, energy efficiency improved\nfrom 0 to 0.8% (in terms of specific indicators).\nThe goal is to achieve significant results by 2025.\nThe potential savings from energy-efficient solutions\nin DCs are estimated at $3.5\U20134 million by 2030.\nDevelopment of digital\nservices and infrastructure\nThe Company is actively developing solutions in the\nareas of:\n\U097b Internet of Things (IoT) to reduce the carbon\n\U097b\nfootprint;\n\U097b Smart grids and remote monitoring;\n\U097b\n\U097b Digital modeling of telecom infrastructure\n\U097b\nto optimize energy consumption;\n\U097b Commercialization of carbon offsets through climate\n\U097b\nprojects.\nRenewable energy\ndevelopment\nAccess to sustainable\nfinancing\nTransition to renewable energy sources and reduced\ndependence on carbon-intensive fuels. Under the\nESG Strategy through 2032, the Company considers\nincreasing the share of renewables from the current\n0% to 10\U201315%. Fuel and emission offset savings may\nreach up to $5 million over the long term.\nIncreased attractiveness to ESG investors, issuance\nof green bonds, and financing for climate-focused\nprojects.\nIntegrated Annual Report / 2024\n89\nThe total economic benefit from realizing climate\nopportunities could exceed $20 million by 2060.\nAs part of the climate analysis, a set\nof recommendations was developed to strengthen the\nCompany\U2019s resilience to climate risks. SUSTAINABLE DEVELOPMENT REPORT Integrated Annual Report / 2024\n90\nClimate rIsk Management\nClimate risk management in the Company is carried\nout within the corporate risk management system\nand is integrated into the unified Risk Registry.\nEnvironmental/climate risk is categorized under\noperational risks and covers factors such as violations\nof environmental legislation, waste management issues,\nand insufficient environmental oversight. Climate risks\nare regularly reviewed during updates of the risk map,\ntaking into account likelihood and impact magnitude.\nMitigation and management measures are developed\nfor key risks.\nCateGORIes OF Climate RISKS and OppORTunITIes\nThe assessment covers both transition risks (regulatory\nchanges, market and technological shifts, investor\nESG expectations) and physical risks (extreme weather\nevents, overheating, floods, power supply disruptions).\nThe analysis considers the geographic distribution and\nclimate vulnerability of Company assets.\nClimate risk identification and assessment involved the\nfollowing elements:\n1. Stage one: Assessment of external climate and\neconomic environment:\n\U2022\nHistorical and current climate trends (temperature,\nprecipitation, wind loads);\n\U2022\nApproach to Climate Risk Identification and Assessment\nDynamics of global and regional climate factors;\n\U2022\nKey demographic, technological, legal, political, and\neconomic drivers;\nThe Company employed a structured and scientifically\n\U2022\nPotential changes in supply chains, service demand,\ngrounded approach to identifying and assessing climate\nand consumer behavior.\nrisks, aligned with international TCFD recommendations,\nas well as IPCC methodologies, guidance from the\nEuropean Bank for Reconstruction and Development\n2. SUSTAINABLE DEVELOPMENT REPORT 3. Kazakhtelecom JSC applied a model combination\nbased on the Representative Concentration Pathways\n(RCP) developed by the Intergovernmental Panel\non Climate Change (IPCC), along with the NZE2050\n(Net Zero Emissions 2050) scenario. The RCP2.6,\nRCP4.5, and RCP8.5 scenarios were used to evaluate\nconsequences of various global warming levels and\ntheir impact on infrastructure, energy consumption,\nand operational resilience:\n\U2022\n\U2022\n\U2022\nRCP 2.6 \U2014 low-carbon pathway (1.5\U20132\U00b0C goal);\nRCP 4.5 \U2014 intermediate emissions level;\nRCP 8.5 \U2014 high-emissions scenario with intensified\nphysical consequences.\nThe NZE2050 scenario focuses on achieving carbon\nneutrality by 2050 and was used to assess transition\nrisks related to climate policy, technological changes,\nand market expectations.\nIntegrated Annual Report / 2024\n1 2\nAssess materiality of climate-\nrelated risks:\nIdentify and define range of\nscenarios:\n\U097b Market and technological changes\n\U097b\n\U097b Reputational risks\n\U097b\n\U097b Political and and capabilities legal risks\n\U097b\n\U097b Physical risks\n\U097b\nScenarios that include a range of transitional and\nphysical risks relevant to the Company.\nAssessment of the Company\U2019s current and future\nclimate-related risks. Their\nimpact on cost structure and investment plans was\nconsidered.\nFor each climate risk, scale and likelihood of impact\nwere determined, taking into account the scenario,\nsite sensitivity, and reliance on external resources.\nThe model factored in potential increases in electricity\ncosts, need for facility modernization, and adaptation-\nrelated expenditures.\nAs a result, priority zones and assets most vulnerable\nto climate impacts were identified\U2013primarily those\nlocated in the southern regions of Kazakhstan, where\nrisks of overheating and energy disruptions are\nexpected to rise.\n4. SUSTAINABLE DEVELOPMENT REPORT Kazakhtelecom JSC systematically works to improve\nthe energy efficiency of its data centers (DCs),\nrecognizing their critical role in supporting the country\U2019s\ndigital infrastructure. A top priority is reducing specific\nenergy consumption while increasing computing capacity\nand system reliability.\nTo improve energy efficiency, the Company plans\nto modernize its DCs, including the installation of new\nequipment and capacity expansion within existing\nfacilities. Particular attention is paid to the summer\nseason, when the load on cooling systems increases \U2014\nthis period requires enhanced energy efficiency and\nsystem reliability to maintain stable IT infrastructure\noperations.\nFrom 2021 to 2023, the total energy consumption\nof data centers demonstrated a steady\ndecrease \U2014 in 2023, consumption dropped by 8.2%\ncompared to 2021. However, despite the positive trend\nin energy consumption, the share of renewable energy\nsources (RES) in the energy mix remains at 0%. This\nindicates potential for transitioning to more sustainable\nenergy sources and the opportunity to integrate\nrenewable solutions into the data center energy supply\narchitecture.\nKazakhtelecom JSC is considering a phased transition\nto RES as part of its medium-term climate strategy. This\nwould help reduce the Company\U2019s carbon footprint and\nenhance the resilience of its digital infrastructure.\nIntegrated Annual Report / 2024\n94\nEneRGy eFFICIency in data centeRS\nOF JSC KazakhteleCOm, %\nThe Company views its current performance indicators\nas benchmarks for further development. SUSTAINABLE DEVELOPMENT REPORT Recruitment\nKazakhtelecom JSC carries out the recruitment\nprocedure in accordance with the Rules of Selecting\nPersonnel of Kazakhtelecom JSC. Recruitment for\nvacant positions and working professions in the\nCompany is carried out by structural divisions of the\nGeneral HR Service Centre and Employee Experience\nManagement Service.\nPrinciples of personnel selection:\n\U097b recruitment planning based on business needs;\n\U097b\n\U097b clear and transparent selection criteria based on the\n\U097b\nrequirements to the position and the Competence\nModel;\n\U097b transparent tender procedures;\n\U097b\n\U097b professionalism, personal qualities of the candidate\n\U097b\nand his/her compliance with the qualification\nrequirements and competencies for the position;\n\U097b reasonableness of decisions taken based\n\U097b\non the meritocracy principle;\n\U097b use of candidates evaluation methods that are\n\U097b\nrelevant for each position, making it possible to make\nobjective decisions when hiring personnel;\n\U097b non-discrimination, professional, open and respectful\n\U097b\nattitude towards all candidates;\n\U097b compliance with laws of the Republic of Kazakhstan;\n\U097b\n\U097b rational use of resources for attracting and recruiting\n\U097b\npersonnel.\nPersonnel selection is carried out on a competitive\nbasis. In-house candidates, including those in the\npersonnel reserve, have priority when filling a vacant\nposition. Applicants for search and selection of qualified\nspecialists can be:\n\U097b the Company\U2019s employees, including reservists in the\n\U097b\npersonnel reserve of Kazakhtelecom JSC;\n\U097b employees of Kazakhtelecom JSC\U2019s Group\n\U097b\nof companies;\n\U097b employees of Samruk-Kazyna JSC Group;\n\U097b\nGRI 404-1\nNumber OF newly hIRed employees, peRSOns\nCategory Total for the Company: By gender group:\n- Women - Men By age group:\n- Less than 30 years - 30-50 years - More than 50 years Integrated Annual Report / 2024\n\U097b candidates participating in the competition for\n\U097b\na vacant position;\n\U097b graduates of universities, senior students.\n\U097b\nThe Company has adopted an Equal Opportunity,\nInclusion and Diversity Policy, one of the key principles\nof which is to strive to build diverse teams and promote\ndiversity initiatives, including prioritising local hiring\nas well as targeted recruitment.\nIf necessary, the Company selects external candidates.\nThe Company uses the following tools to search for\npotential new employees:\n\U097b electronic database of candidates formed on the\n\U097b\nUnified Online Recruitment Platform Samruk Qyzmet\n(https://qsamruk.kz/);\n\U097b electronic CV database generated by the Company;\n\U097b\n\U097b specialised sites with CV databases (Qyzmet.kz,\n\U097b\nKz.jooble.org and others);\n2022 2023 2024\n2,175 1,809 1,947\n715 605 634\n1,460 1,204 1,313\n1,216 928 956\n813 718 851\n146 163 140\n101\n\U097b social networks (Facebook, LinkedIn and others);\n\U097b\n\U097b electronic database of graduates of young specialists\n\U097b\ndevelopment/talent management programmes\nimplemented by the Company/Samruk-Kazyna JSC.\nIn 2024, 1,947 new employees were hired by the Company.\nAmong them, 13 individuals were selected from the\nCompany\U2019s Talent Pool. It covers\nlong-term, medium-term, and operational planning.\nEmployees are assigned responsibility for\nachieving results in key business areas, with\nperformance monitoring aligned to strategic goals,\nobjectives, and initiatives. The Company ensures\na balance between financial and non-financial KPIs\nand monitors progress through regular (quarterly/annual)\nperformance evaluations, including factor analysis and\nthe development of recommendations.\nThe performance planning and evaluation cycle\nis designed for continuous performance management\nthroughout the calendar year. A key condition for\nbonus payments based on results is the availability\nof consolidated net profit, calculated taking into account\nthe planned bonus payment fund.\nThe Company has implemented an annual Employee\nRating system based on performance and competency\ndevelopment. This rating system categorizes employees\non the Company\U2019s talent map from \U201cineffective\U201d to \U201chigh\nleadership potential\U201d to inform personnel decisions.\nChanges introduced to the performance evaluation\nsystem in 2024:\n\U097b Updated \U201cRules on Current Bonuses for Employees\n\U097b\nof Kazakhtelecom JSC Branches\U201d;\n\U097b Introduced quarterly KPIs for all employees, as per\n\U097b\nthe updated evaluation rules;\n\U097b Automated the process for setting and calculating\n\U097b\nthe Labor Participation Coefficient (LPC).\nThe Company has also implemented the Individual\nDevelopment Plan (IDP) system, allowing each employee\nto focus on enhancing their knowledge, skills, and\nperformance.\nIn the reporting period, 1,756 employees (9.6% of the\ntotal headcount) were covered by regular performance\nand career development evaluations.\nGRI 404-3\nNumber OF employees COvered by regular peRFORmance and career development evaluaTIOns, PeRSOns\nIndicator 2022 2023 2024\nKazakhtelecom JSC 530 1,628 1,756\nBy gender group:\n- Women 173 716 598\n- Men 357 912 1,158\nBy employee category:\n- Managers 234 638 673\n- Specialists 296 990 1,083\n- Workers 0 0 0\n4. SUSTAINABLE DEVELOPMENT REPORT Integrated Annual Report / 2024\n106\nSoCIal Stability\nDuring the reporting period, the Company continued\nits efforts to maintain social stability. Heads\nof HR functions in the divisions and branches\nof Kazakhtelecom JSC held meetings with employees\nto discuss matters of social and labor relations, payroll,\nand social support.\nThe Company has established an effective\ncommunication channel between employees and\ntop management in the format of online conferences,\nwhich includes the following procedures:\n\U097b initial collection of a pool of questions;\n\U097b\n\U097b moderation of the question pool by the\n\U097b\nCommunications Department of Kazakhtelecom JSC;\n\U097b a live broadcast with the Chairman of the\n\U097b\nManagement Board.\nThe group of companies of Samruk-Kazyna JSC\nholds an annual monitoring of the social environment\nin production teams. To identify hidden social\ntensions in a timely manner and manage this process,\nKazakhtelecom JSC, in cooperation with the Private\nInstitution \U201cCenter for Social Interaction and\nCommunications\U201d, conducts a sociological study called\nSamruk Research Services (SRS). Based on the survey\nresults and sociologists\U2019 recommendations, an annual\nAction Plan to address areas of concern is developed\nand approved.\nIn 2024, the Center for Social Interaction and\nCommunications conducted an SRS index study.\nThe total score amounted to 68%, exceeding the\nthreshold KPI of Kazakhtelecom JSC, which is set\nat 60%.\nThe Engagement Index measures satisfaction with\ninfrastructure, workload, remuneration and social\nbenefits, loyalty, communication, development and\ncareer opportunities, and recognition by leadership.\nThe Social Well-being Index captures self-assessment\nof current and dynamic well-being, including social,\nfinancial, health, and environmental quality aspects.\nThe Social Calm Index reflects the level of social\ntension, employees\U2019 perception of the protection\nof their rights, conflict levels within the team, and\nprotest sentiments, including readiness to participate\nin protests and loyalty toward those who do.\nAs part of the 2024 Action Plan to address areas\nof concern, developed based on SRS results,\nKazakhtelecom JSC implemented a set of measures\naimed at improving working conditions, enhancing\nemployee motivation, and developing corporate culture\nin the following areas:\n\U097b Enhancing communication and openness\n\U097b\nin interactions;\n\U097b Improving social and living conditions;\n\U097b\n\U097b Providing necessary resources to employees;\n\U097b\n\U097b Staff training and development;\n\U097b\n\U097b Corporate culture development and employee\n\U097b\nengagement;\n\U097b Implementation of the Well-Being program;\n\U097b\n\U097b Raising employee awareness of trade union and\n\U097b\nOmbudsman activities.\nThe total srs index score is a composite of the following three sub-indICes\n68%\n54%\n84%\nEngagement Index\nSocial Well-being Index\nSocial Calm Index\n4. SUSTAINABLE DEVELOPMENT REPORT Employee SoCIal Support\nGRI 2-30, 404-2 Kazakhtelecom JSC maintains a system of social\nsupport for employees that ensures comfortable and\nsafe working conditions. The Collective Agreement\nof Kazakhtelecom JSC covers 92% of the Company\U2019s\nemployees.\nIn accordance with the Collective Agreement, the\nCompany continued to provide the following types\nof social support in 2024, regardless of the nature\nof employment (permanent or temporary):\n\U097b life insurance;\n\U097b\n\U097b medical care;\n\U097b\n\U097b parental leave;\n\U097b\n\U097b pension programs.\n\U097b\nAdditionally, under the Collective Agreement\nof Kazakhtelecom JSC, the Company provides support\nto employees in cases of downsizing and retirement,\nincluding the opportunity to transfer to vacant positions,\nearly retirement based on service duration, paid time off\nfor job searching, and lump-sum payments upon dismissal\nor retirement.\n92%\nCompany\U2019s employees\nare covered by the Collective Agreement\nof JSC \U201cKazakhtelecom\U201d\nGRI 402-1\nThe minimum notice period for termination of employment\ncontracts due to workforce or position reductions,\nas per the Labour Code of the Republic of Kazakhstan,\nis 4 weeks (30 calendar days). In accordance with the\nCollective Agreement adopted by Kazakhtelecom JSC,\nthis period exceeds the minimum legal requirements and\nis set at 45 calendar days.\nGRI 401-2\nIn addition to standard employee benefits, the Company\nhas introduced a \U201cBenefits Cafeteria\U201d system that\nallows employees to independently determine the\nstructure and content of their benefits package within\nthe limits of allocated funds and the list of available\nbenefits.\nThe \U201cBenefits Cafeteria\U201d concept applies to employees\nholding the following positions:\n\U097b Managing Directors of the Head Office, Chief\n\U097b\nTreasurer, HR Director, Director for Customer\nExperience Management, and Business Line Directors\nof branches who report directly to the General\nDirectors of the branches;\n\U097b Heads of structural subdivisions of the Head Office.\n\U097b\nThe \U201cBenefits Cafeteria\U201d includes the following\ncategories:\n\U2022\n\U2022\n\U2022\nexpansion of voluntary medical insurance\ncoverage;\nreimbursement of educational course/program\ncosts for employees and/or their children;\nreimbursement of costs for health resort\ntreatment (excluding those covered under VMI),\namong others.\nIntegrated Annual Report / 2024\nOne of the Company\U2019s key social programs is the\n\U201cDEMEU\U201d program, which provides assistance to large\nfamilies, families with children with disabilities, and\nfamilies that have adopted more than two children.\nIn 2024, the program was expanded to include the\n\U201csingle-parent family\U201d category and financial support\nfor caregiving for close relatives. Additionally, under\nthe Program, social support is provided to employees\non A8\U2013B4 grades in the form of reimbursement for\nfinal-year tuition expenses in colleges/universities.\nWithin the \U201cDEMEU\U201d program, Company employees\nreceive payments to cover expenses related to the\nrehabilitation of children with disabilities, special\neducation programs, attendance at special correctional\ninstitutions, travel vouchers to children\U2019s wellness\ncamps and sanatoriums (for children with disabilities),\nand financial assistance for medications, school meals,\nand more.\n1,600\nemployees\nreceived payments under the \U201cdemeu\U201d\nprogram totaling in 2024\n>300\nKZT million\n107\nOne of the focus areas of the Employee Experience\nstrategy is ensuring the well-being and health\nof Kazakhtelecom JSC employees. In 2024, the\nCompany continued to implement the Well-Being\nProgram aimed at monitoring employee health and\npreventing illnesses, while promoting a healthy lifestyle.\nBased on employee health monitoring results for 2023,\na Comprehensive Program on Well-Being and Health\nwas developed in February 2024.\nDuring the year, as part of the Program on Monitoring\nand Preventing Employee Illnesses, a set of activities\nwas implemented to protect employee health and\nreduce work-related risks. The year-end results showed\na positive trend in both the Health Index and the Well-\nBeing Index. According to a survey, job satisfaction\nincreased by 24%, which may be attributed to improved\nworking conditions, enhanced stress management\nskills, a stronger moral climate, and the development\nof corporate culture.
