SUSTAINABLE DEVELOPMENT REPORT Integrated Annual Report / 2024\nRESpect FOR huMAn rights and equal oppORtunitiES\nManagement ApproachProtection and Promotion of Human rIghts\nGRI 3-3, 406-1 Kazakhtelecom JSC is committed to protecting and\nupholding human rights, creating equal opportunities for\nall employees, and preventing conditions that may lead\nto gender inequality or any form of discrimination.\nThe Company informs employees, contractors, and other\nstakeholders about its policies and principles of good\nfaith business conduct.\nKazakhtelecom JSC views the protection of human rights\nand the provision of equal opportunities as an integral\npart of its operations. The foundation of this work is laid\nout in the following key documents:\n\U097b Human Rights Policy\n\U097b\n\U097b Policy on Equal Opportunities, Inclusivity, and Diversity.\n\U097b\nGRI 2-23\nThe Policy sets forth the principles that guide the\nCompany in upholding human rights at all stages of its\noperations.\nKey principles of the Human Rights Policy include:\n\U097b The Company complies with the legislation\n\U097b\nof the Republic of Kazakhstan, as well as with\ninternational human rights norms and standards,\nincluding the Universal Declaration of Human\nRights adopted by the UN General Assembly,\nthe UN Global Compact, and the ILO Declaration\non Fundamental Principles and Rights at Work.\n\U097b The Company believes that all individuals are\n\U097b\nfree and equal in dignity and rights, regardless\nof gender, race, skin color, nationality, language,\norigin, age, place of residence, religious beliefs,\npersonal convictions, membership or non-\nmembership in public associations or social groups,\nproperty or family status, social or professional\nstanding, or any other factors not related\nto professional qualities.\n\U097b The Company does not tolerate any form\n\U097b\nof discrimination or violation of human dignity,\nnor any physical or psychological violence in the\nworkplace.\n\U097b The Company opposes forced labor, child labor, and\n\U097b\nhuman trafficking.\n\U097b The Company ensures the protection of human\n\U097b\ndignity and the inviolability of private life.\n\U097b The Company adheres to the principle of zero\n\U097b\ntolerance for corruption.\n\U097b The Company strives to develop a human rights\n\U097b\nrisk management procedure in line with international\nbest practices.\nThese Policies are available on the Company\U2019s website\ntelecom.kz in the \U201cSustainable Development\U201d section, under\nthe \U201cHuman Rights and Equal Opportunities\U201d subsection.\n114\n\U097b The Company aims to identify and prevent any\n\U097b\nadverse human rights impacts within its operations.\n\U097b The Human Rights Policy applies\n\U097b\nto Kazakhtelecom JSC employees, shareholders,\nclients, and other stakeholders.\nThe Company\U2019s Human Rights Policy applies\nto Kazakhtelecom JSC employees, shareholders,\nclients, and other stakeholders.\n4. SUSTAINABLE DEVELOPMENT REPORT Equal Opportunities\nThe Company continues to implement the \U201cPolicy\non Equal Opportunities, Inclusivity, and Diversity,\U201d\nwhich is aimed at promoting practices of equality,\ninclusivity, and diversity, considering individual\ncharacteristics, and preventing discrimination\nat all levels of employment. The Policy aligns\nwith international best practices and standards\nand complies with the legislation of the Republic\nof Kazakhstan.\nKey principles of the Policy include:\n\U097b Compliance with the legislation of the Republic\n\U097b\nof Kazakhstan and adherence to the principles\nset forth in the Equal Remuneration Convention\n(Convention No. 100) and the 1958 Discrimination\n(Employment and Occupation) Convention\n(Convention No. 111).\n\U097b Ensuring equal opportunities, inclusivity, and\n\U097b\ndiversity for all employees.\n\U097b Providing employees with social guarantees\n\U097b\nin accordance with the legislation of the Republic\nof Kazakhstan.\n\U097b Cultivating a corporate culture based on mutual\n\U097b\nrespect, free of social biases and cultural barriers.\n\U097b Providing a decent, safe, and comfortable working\n\U097b\nenvironment in which every employee feels\nrespected, accepted, and heard, and is empowered\nand entitled to fulfill their job responsibilities.\n\U097b Encouraging transparency in labor relations and\n\U097b\nsupporting employee development and career\nbuilding through assistance and opportunities for\nprofessional growth.\n\U097b Promoting team diversity and supporting diversity\n\U097b\ndevelopment initiatives, including prioritizing\nthe hiring of local candidates and implementing\ntargeted hiring programs.\nIntegrated Annual Report / 2024\nThe Policy applies to Kazakhtelecom JSC employees,\nshareholders, clients, and other stakeholders.\nThe Company ensures equal opportunities for\nemployees in selection, recruitment, assessment,\npromotion, development, training, and compensation\nprocesses.\nA collective agreement is in force at the Company,\nbased on the principles of social partnership,\nfostering cooperation between employees and the\nCompany. The agreement is aimed at improving work\nefficiency and protecting employees\U2019 social and labor\ninterests. It outlines the general positions of the\nparties regarding the regulation of labor relations,\nremuneration, employment, social guarantees, and\nbenefits. The Company participates in negotiations\non drafting, amending, and supplementing the\ncollective agreement, observes negotiation deadlines,\nensures the operation of joint commissions, and\nprovides the information necessary for the negotiation\nprocess. The Company strictly complies with the\nterms of the collective agreement. In accordance with\nlabor law, every employee has the right to participate\nin collective bargaining through their representatives\nand to review the signed agreement.\nKazakhtelecom JSC ensures equal pay regardless\nof position or gender. The Company\U2019s average monthly\nwage is not dependent on job title and is determined\nin accordance with the Company\U2019s compensation rules.\nMore information about the Company\U2019s compensation\napproach and key 2023 results can be found in the\n\U201cEmployee Relations\U201d section.\n115\nGRI 406-1\nThe Company monitors the prevention\nof discrimination on any grounds and ensures a fair\nand equitable approach to compensation. No incidents\nof discrimination were recorded at Kazakhtelecom JSC\nduring the reporting period.\nAs part of key national and corporate initiatives\non human rights and gender equality, Samruk-\nKazyna JSC is initiating the development\nof a 2025 Action Plan aimed at upholding human\nrights and promoting equal opportunities, including for\nKazakhtelecom JSC.\nThis Plan will serve as a logical continuation of a number\nof strategic documents, including the Human Rights\nAction Plan, the Equal Rights and Opportunities Plan for\nMen and Women, as well as the Action Plan for the 2025\nYear of Skilled Trades.\nIn addition, within the framework of the memorandum\nbetween Samruk-Kazyna JSC and the United Nations\nDevelopment Programme, the Managing Directors for\nSocial and Labor Relations of portfolio companies signed\nDeclarations of Intent confirming their commitment\nto the principles of human rights and gender equality.\nThe Plan under development will be mandatory for\nimplementation by all Portfolio Companies of the\nFund, including Kazakhtelecom JSC, and will form the\nfoundation for consistent and systematic work in this\narea across the entire group.\n4. SUSTAINABLE DEVELOPMENT REPORT Employee Engagement in oCCupational Safety Management\nGRI 403-2, 403-4\nKazakhtelecom JSC recognizes the vital role\nemployees play in occupational safety management\nand in developing a strong safety culture. The Company\nactively involves its personnel in the design,\nimplementation, and evaluation of the occupational\nhealth and safety system. Occupational safety and\nhealth committees have been established in all branches\nand at the Head Office, where employees collaborate\nto ensure compliance with OHS requirements, prevent\nworkplace injuries and occupational diseases, and\ninspect working conditions and safety measures.\nIn crisis situations, the Company forms a task force\nwith participation from the OSD and the Civil Defense\nHeadquarters to investigate and eliminate the crisis.\nKazakhtelecom JSC conducts monthly meetings with\nbranch directors, structural unit representatives, and\ncontractors to discuss ongoing and new OHS initiatives\nand programs. It has also introduced a practice\nof beginning all administrative and production meetings\nwith a brief discussion on safety and occupational health.\nCompany employees also participated in sharing\nbest practices through the HSE Committee platform\norganized by Samruk-Kazyna JSC at production\nsites of portfolio companies, with the aim of further\nreplicating best practices at Kazakhtelecom JSC.\nAdditionally, an internal audit covering occupational\nsafety and compliance with workplace standards was\nconducted across all structural units.\n\U201cOccupational Health and Safety Card\U201d\nProgram\nSince 2022, Kazakhtelecom JSC has implemented the\nstandard \U201cOccupational Health and Safety Card\U201d Program\n(OHS cards), designed to increase employee engagement\nin improving the OHS system.\nThe Program focuses on identifying and reporting\nhazardous production factors, unsafe working conditions,\nunsafe employee behavior, potentially dangerous\nsituations, and near misses. It also allows employees\nto propose improvements in OHS.\nThe Program\U2019s objective is not only to eliminate and\ncontrol risks of injury or environmental/property damage\nbut also to involve employees in enhancing production\ndiscipline and promoting a safety culture through the use\nof OHS cards at every workplace, site, and facility.\nOHS cards are used to report and communicate\non all matters related to occupational health, safety,\nand environmental protection. The system also allows\ntracking the resolution of reported issues, ensuring\ntimely follow-up.\n172\nemployees\nparticipated in Ipt activities in 2024\nIntegrated Annual Report / 2024\n117\nIn 2024, the top three risk areas identified were:\n\U097b Personal protective equipment (PPE) provision;\n\U097b\n\U097b Health and hygiene;\n\U097b\n\U097b Workplace ergonomics.\n\U097b\nTo enhance engagement of non-OSD employees, the Com-\npany decided to train all staff on how to complete and regis-\nter OHS cards. SUSTAINABLE DEVELOPMENT REPORT Improvement\nof the oCCupational health and\nsafety management system\nGRI 403-1\nThe Company is committed to aligning with\ninternational standards in occupational health and\nsafety. Occupational health and safety management\nsystems have been implemented in the Company\nin accordance with globally recognized standards.\nThe OHS and industrial safety management system\nestablishes uniform requirements based on the ILO-\nOSH 2001 Guidelines on Occupational Safety and\nHealth Management Systems and the ISO 45001:2018\ninternational standard.\nThe Company continuously enhances its occupational\nhealth and industrial safety management system in line\nwith the requirements of the ILO-OSH standard and its\nnational equivalent, ST RK ISO 45001\U20132018.\nIn 2024, in order to improve workplace safety and\ncomfort, certification of 1,428 production facilities\nwas carried out. Based on the results of measurements\nof harmful and hazardous occupational factors,\na comprehensive set of corrective actions was\nimplemented. An internal audit was conducted to assess\nproduction safety and compliance of workplaces with\noccupational health and safety requirements across all\nstructural units of the Company.\n1,504\nKZT million\ntotal investments in industrial safety and\noccupational health in 2024\nrIsk assessment\nGRI 403-2\nThe process of managing key OHS risks is an integral\npart of the Company\U2019s corporate risk management\nsystem, as well as its occupational health and\nsafety (OHS) management system. The assessment\nof unacceptable hazards and risks is carried out\nin accordance with the approved documented procedure\n\U201cIdentification of Hazards, Environmental Aspects\nand Risk Assessment. Procedure for Defining Control\nMeasures.\U201d\nTo eliminate the risks of accidents and incidents in the\nworkplace, modernization and major repairs of linear and\nstation telecommunication facilities were carried out\nin accordance with the Annual Plan.\nOccupational injuries are defined as one of the key risks\nin the Company\U2019s Risk Register. A set of measures has\nbeen developed to prevent the realization of this risk and\nto mitigate its consequences.\nTo identify work-related hazards and assess risks, the\nCompany prepares action plans for key risk events and\nprovides up-to-date status reports on key risk indicators\nbased on data on occupational injuries, industrial\naccidents, and internal OHS controls. The Company\nhas also approved a Register of Significant Hazards\nand Unacceptable Risks. Furthermore, the likelihood\nand impact of risks are analyzed and assessed, with\nrisk mitigation measures reviewed in light of the current\nsituation.\nIn addition, the Company\U2019s Collective Agreement provides\na mechanism that allows employees to refuse to perform\nwork if they believe that continuing such work could lead\nto injury or harm to health. The agreement also contains\nprovisions that guarantee protection against retaliation\nfor exercising this right.\nIntegrated Annual Report / 2024\n118\nGRI 403-2, 403-9\nKazakhtelecom JSC regularly identifies and assesses\nproject-related risks and potential adverse impacts on the\nhealth and safety of the population in its areas of presence.\nBased on the results of these assessments, protective and\npreventive measures are developed. Where necessary, the\nCompany cooperates with relevant government authorities\nand other stakeholders regarding mitigation actions and\nplans.\nAs part of the hazard identification and risk assessment\nprocedure, the Company takes into account the\nroutine activities of all personnel, human behaviour and\ncapabilities, hazards identified near or outside the work\nareas, infrastructure, equipment and materials, and\ntechnological processes. Risk management activities have\nbeen defined and are implemented across the Company.\n4. SUSTAINABLE DEVELOPMENT REPORT Prevention of oCCupational injuries\nGRI 403-7\nThe Company pays great attention to the proactive\nprevention and mitigation of adverse impacts on the\nhealth and safety of employees, contractors, and local\ncommunities.\nThe list of KPIs for heads of the Company\U2019s regional\nbranches in the area of occupational safety includes\nthe Lost Time Injury Frequency (LTIF) rate.\nThe Company develops and implements measures\naimed at preventing occupational injuries.\nAn analysis of the causes of occupational injuries and\nroad traffic accidents is carried out, followed by the\ndistribution of informational bulletins to branches\ncontaining preventive and corrective measures.\nIn addition, the circumstances and causes of incidents\nare discussed with employees across all departments,\nand unscheduled safety briefings are conducted.\nEach year, the Company implements a Zero Injury Plan,\nwith quarterly progress reports submitted for review\nby the Board of Directors.\nTo adopt leading practices, the Company monitors\nthe use of proactive safety tools such as behavioural\nsafety audits, with registration and investigation\nof hazardous conditions, unsafe actions, and\nnear misses.\nThe Company has also improved the efficiency\nof contractor management. This includes the development of an internal regulatory\ndocument governing the management of contractor\norganisations, as well as the introduction of kick-\noff meetings with contractors to ensure the safe\nexecution of work at production facilities.\nTo raise awareness of the importance of seatbelt\nuse and reduce injury rates from road accidents,\nKazakhtelecom employees were trained using\na collision simulator.\nThe Company does not maintain statistical records\nof injuries among contractor personnel engaged under\nservice agreements.\nIn response to the need to enhance fire safety, comply\nwith the legislation of the Republic of Kazakhstan, and\nreduce the risk of fire incidents, Kazakhtelecom JSC\nhas adopted a Fire Safety Policy.\nIntegrated Annual Report / 2024\n119\nInjury rates among employees of Kazakhtelecom JSC\nGRI 403-9\nInjury rates among employees OF KazakhteleCOm JSC*\nFor all employees 2022 2023 2024\nNumber of work-related fatalities (units) 0 0 0\nWork-related fatality rate (%) 0 0 0\nNumber of severe work-related injuries (units) 2 1 4\nSevere work-related injury rate (%) 0.06 0.03 0.12\nNumber of occupational injuries (units) 2 6 6\nLost Time Injury Frequency Rate (LTIFR) 0.06 0.19 0.19\nTotal number of working hours (man-hours) 34,007,902 31,780,000 31,308,380\n* The reported data covers 100% of the Company\U2019s employees. SUSTAINABLE DEVELOPMENT REPORT The Company operates a video-based training\nprogramme for responsible managers on occupational\nhealth and industrial safety (OHS) matters. As part\nof the programme, employees are shown video materials\non the following topics:\n\U097b performing high-risk work in areas near power lines\n\U097b\nand using special equipment;\n\U097b methods and techniques that ensure employee\n\U097b\nsafety;\n\U097b providing first aid in the event of workplace\n\U097b\naccidents.\nThis video training programme is implemented across\nall structural units and divisions of the Company, with\ncontinuous monitoring, analysis, and decision-making\naimed at improving its effectiveness. This training\nformat helps enhance employee performance in the\ncourse of operational activities and minimise existing\nworkplace risks.\nPrevention of oCCupational\ndiseases and health\nprotection\nGRI 403-3, 403-6\nAs employee well-being is a key priority for\nKazakhtelecom JSC, special attention is paid to their\nhealth.\nAs part of the employee benefits package, full medical\ninsurance is provided. Employees also have access\nto wellness and sanatorium-resort treatment\nprogrammes in accordance with the terms of the\nCollective Agreement, as well as the Demeu programme.\nRegular pre-employment, periodic, and\nunscheduled medical examinations are conducted\nfor employees. Based on the results, if necessary,\nemployees are referred for in-depth preventive\ncheck-ups. Production personnel required\nto undergo mandatory medical exams are not permitted\nto begin work if the examination is not completed.\nIn accordance with the Labor Code of the Republic\nof Kazakhstan, employees of contracting organizations\nengaged in high-risk work or operating machinery and\nequipment are also subject to mandatory pre- and post-\nshift medical screenings.\nAs part of the Company\U2019s corporate Well-Being\nprogram, a number of health-related activities\nare conducted to prevent illnesses. To assess\ncardiovascular risk among employees, screenings\nare carried out using the Cardiovisor device.\nBased on the results, employees receive\nconsultations with physicians and personalized\nrecommendations. Wellness assessments are\nalso conducted using the Mediscreen device\nto identify musculoskeletal health issues, with medical\nguidance provided accordingly.\nIn addition to these core initiatives, employees\nof Kazakhtelecom JSC participated in a webinar titled\n\U201cHow to Boost Your Energy and Strengthen Immunity.\U201d\nThe Company also organized Health Days and physical\nactivities aimed at supporting and improving employees\U2019\nphysical condition.\nIntegrated Annual Report / 2024\noCCupational Health and\nIndustrial Safety Management\nin Contracting Organizations\nGRI 403-3, 403-6\nContracting organizations performing work at the\nCompany\U2019s sites are required to comply with applicable\nenvironmental protection and occupational safety\nstandards and regulations.\nKazakhtelecom JSC places great importance\non engaging with suppliers of goods, works, and services\nin the context of managing occupational health and\nsafety (OHS) aspects. SUSTAINABLE DEVELOPMENT REPORT lOcal cOMMunitiES\nManagement Approach\nGRI 3-3\nThe Company is committed to contributing to the\ndevelopment of the regions where it operates. We provide\nlocal populations with quality telecommunications and\ninternet access, help reduce the digital divide between\nurban and rural areas, and support those in urgent need.\nThe key document governing engagement with local\ncommunities is the Local Community Engagement Policy.\nThis Policy establishes a unified approach for\nKazakhtelecom JSC in managing relationships with local\nexecutive authorities, civil society organizations, and\nlocal populations in the Company\U2019s regions of operation.\nIt is aimed at maintaining constructive and positive\nrelations with these stakeholders.\nThe Policy is based on the principles outlined in the\nfollowing international instruments: the United Nations\nGlobal Compact, the Universal Declaration of Human\nRights, and the International Labour Organization\nConventions. It also aligns with the UN Sustainable\nDevelopment Goals.\nThe core principles of the Policy include:\n\U097b Contribute to the socio-economic development of the\n\U097b\nregions where the Company operates through its\nbusiness activities.\n\U097b Promote the improvement of quality of life\n\U097b\nfor members of local communities in areas of presence.\n\U097b Maintain constructive relationships with local\n\U097b\ncommunities by taking into account their opinions,\ninterests, perspectives, and preferences.\n\U097b Comply with the laws and regulations of the Republic\n\U097b\nof Kazakhstan.\n\U097b Minimize social and environmental risks and impacts\n\U097b\non local populations in the regions where the Company\noperates.\nGRI 203-1\nThe Company does not have dedicated departments\nresponsible for implementing local community\nengagement programs. SUSTAINABLE DEVELOPMENT REPORT Flood Relief Assistance\nIn 2024, Kazakhtelecom JSC took prompt and\ncomprehensive support measures in response to the\nlarge-scale floods that affected various regions\nof the Republic of Kazakhstan. The Company did not\nstand aside in the face of this disaster and allocated\nsignificant resources to assist both affected residents\nand its own employees.\nAs part of a decision made by the Board of Directors,\nKazakhtelecom JSC allocated KZT 1 billion through the\nSamruk-Kazyna Trust Fund to provide financial support\nto the affected regions. This decision was part of the\nCompany\U2019s strategic approach to social responsibility\nduring times of crisis.\nSpecial attention was given to supporting internal\nstaff. A total of 112 employees of the Company were\naffected by the floods. Through the work of the Social\nCommission, they received financial assistance during\nthis difficult time, totaling KZT 22.4 million. In addition,\nas a gesture of solidarity, Kazakhtelecom employees\norganized a voluntary fundraising effort, in which\nKZT 35 million was withheld from their salaries and\ndirected to support their affected colleagues.\nThe Company also highly appreciated the contributions\nof its employees who participated in post-flood\nrecovery efforts across the regions. For their active\ninvolvement and dedication, each of the 388 employees\nwas awarded a one-time bonus of KZT 100,000.\nIntegrated Annual Report / 2024\n123\nCompany Engagement with Local Communities\nGRI 2-26, 2-29\nKazakhtelecom JSC takes into account the interests,\nexpectations, and opinions of employees, partners, local\ncommunities, and other stakeholders in the planning and\nimplementation of its projects.\nThe Company regularly engages in constructive and\nrespectful dialogue with local communities, aiming\nto address their needs and minimize potential risks\nassociated with its operations.\nKey methods of engagement with local communities\ninclude:\n\U097b Providing up-to-date information\n\U097b\nthrough media publications about development\nplans and Kazakhtelecom\U2019s performance in the field\nof sustainable development.\n\U097b Conducting surveys and questionnaires via\n\U097b\ncorporate media channels to understand the opinions\nof local communities regarding initiatives planned\nin regions of operation.\n\U097b Addressing inquiries through feedback channels.\n\U097b\n\U097b Planning and implementing social investment and\n\U097b\ncharitable activities as part of socio-economic\nsupport in the regions.\n\U097b Engaging in direct dialogue through participation\n\U097b\nin joint meetings, working groups, and standing\ncommittees with representatives of local\ncommunities.\n\U097b Establishing effective cooperation with local\n\U097b\ngovernment authorities to promote regional\ndevelopment.\nKazakhtelecom JSC actively participates in the\nimplementation of the national \U201cComfortable School\U201d\nproject, aimed at modernizing the country\U2019s educational\ninfrastructure. SUSTAINABLE DEVELOPMENT REPORT Integrated Annual Report / 2024\nMARKEts and cOMpetitionInnovation and nEw tEchnolOGiES\nManagement ApproachManagement ApproachNew Businesses and New Products\nInnovative technologies play an important role in achieving\nthe strategic goals of the Company and contribute\nto the creation of high-quality and user-friendly services\nfor millions of people in Kazakhstan.\nThe implementation of innovative projects and\nthe digital transformation of the Company help\nenhance management efficiency, minimize risks,\nand support alignment with ESG principles and the\nachievement of the UN Sustainable Development Goals.\nKazakhtelecom JSC develops and implements various\ndigital products and solutions for individuals, businesses,\nand the public sector.\nDDoS Attack Protection\nDDoS attack protection is one of the most in-demand\nservices among corporate clients in Kazakhstan.\nThe \U201cDDoS Attack Protection\U201d service comprises a set\nof measures aimed at providing maximum resistance\nto and prevention of DDoS attacks from the Internet,\nGRI 3-3\nThe management of anti-competitive behavior\nat Kazakhtelecom JSC involves a combination\nof legal, ethical, and strategic measures. One of the\nfundamental legislative acts followed by the Company\nis the Law of the Republic of Kazakhstan \U201cOn Natural\nMonopolies.\U201d\nThe Company is included in the national section of the\nState Register of Entities of Natural Monopolies\nand performs the functions of a \U201cuniversal service\U201d\noperator, which subjects its activities to state\nregulation.\nThe antimonopoly regulation of Kazakhtelecom JSC\U2019s\nactivities is overseen by the authorized body for\nnatural monopolies in the telecommunications\nsector \U2014 the Committee for State Control in the\nSphere of Communications, Informatization and\nMass Media under the Ministry of Information and\nCommunications of the Republic of Kazakhstan.\nThe authority for competition protection with respect\nto Kazakhtelecom JSC is exercised by the Committee\nfor Regulation of Natural Monopolies, Protection\nof Competition and Consumer Rights under the Ministry\nof National Economy of the Republic of Kazakhstan.\nAs part of the \U201cEstablishment of a SOC\nand Information Security Services\nfor B2B/B2G\U201d project, two additional\nAntiDDoS scrubbing devices were\ndeployed in Astana using the InlIne\nscheme. These devices provide protection\nagainst internal DDoS attacks for\nKazakhtelecom JSC subscribers.\nPreparations for their commissioning and\nthe development of a product catalog for\nthe service are currently underway.\nGRI 2-27, 206-1\nDuring the reporting period, the Company did not\nrecord any cases related to violations of antimonopoly\nlegislation or other legal actions against the Company\nin connection with obstruction of competition.\nInternet access with cache server integration\nCache servers are part of the infrastructure of the\nlargest content providers \U2014 online games, video hosting\nplatforms, streaming services, and social networks \U2014\nhosted in Kazakhtelecom JSC\U2019s data centers within\nKazakhstan. The product offered by Kazakhtelecom\nprovides Internet access and access to the Company\U2019s\ncached resources for subscribers in the B2O segment.\n129\nbased on solutions from global leaders in the field\nof cybersecurity. The service helps reduce risks\nrelated to the unavailability of public resources due\nto bandwidth saturation or critical equipment overload\ncaused by DDoS attacks.\nIn Almaty and Astana, a hardware\nand software complex for \U201cIntrusion\nProtection\U201d has been deployed, which\nincludes a Next Generation Firewall, Web\nApplication Firewall, Email Protection, and\nSandbox. At present, pilot sales of the\n\U201cFirewall Service\U201d are being conducted.\nUsing this product allows clients and end users\nto significantly reduce the time needed to access\npopular resources. It also helps lower costs associated\nwith the purchase and maintenance of expensive\nequipment such as data storage systems, servers, power\nsupply units, and network infrastructure.\n4. SUSTAINABLE DEVELOPMENT REPORT TelecommunICations Infrastructure and Network Development\nModernization of Backbone Data\nTransmission Network (BDTN)\nExpansion of Network Infrastructure\n(Peering) and Caching Servers to Optimize Content Access\nIn 2024, the implementation of the project \U201cExpansion\nof Port Capacity for Operator Connections\U201d was\ncompleted. During the 2020\U20132024 period, the\nfollowing measures were carried out:\n\U097b Expansion/installation of ASBR (Autonomous System\n\U097b\nBorder Routers) of the backbone data transmission\nnetwork;\n\U097b Expansion of external Internet channels on ASBR\n\U097b\nrouters of the backbone data transmission network;\n\U097b Expansion of port capacity on MX-PE routers of the\n\U097b\nbackbone data transmission network;\n\U097b Expansion of port capacity on MASG routers of the\n\U097b\nMobile Backhaul network;\n\U097b Expansion/modernization of core P-routers (PTX)\n\U097b\nof the backbone data transmission network;\n\U097b Expansion/installation of DWDM backbone channels;\n\U097b\n\U097b Expansion/installation of SpeedTest servers\n\U097b\nto monitor the quality of data transmission services\nacross the backbone data transmission network.\nIn 2024, service edge routers were upgraded.\nAs a result of installation and commissioning works,\ntelecommunications operators can now connect to 100\nGbps ports in the cities of Astana, Almaty, Aktobe,\nShymkent, Karaganda, Atyrau, Taraz, Pavlodar, Kyzylorda,\nSemey, Uralsk, Kostanay, Aktau, and Ust-Kamenogorsk.\nIn 2024, new caching servers were launched for VK,\nCloudFlare, Baishan, Microsoft, and others. The total\nvolume of localized traffic throughput exceeded 5\nTbps. A cluster of high-performance servers was\ndeployed in Pavlodar to support the launch of various\nservices.\nSignificant investments were made in the data center\nin Astana to improve power supply, cooling systems,\ndata transmission equipment, racks, and other\ninfrastructure components. These improvements will\nenable the hosting of a substantial number of caching\nservers in the coming years.\nIn 2024, successful negotiations were held with\nTelegram, resulting in the establishment of a direct\npeering connection at one of the Company\U2019s points\nof presence (POP) with a total capacity of 100G.\nA commercial contract was also successfully\nimplemented with MTS for access to Telegram peering.\nIntegrated Annual Report / 2024\nDNS Service Improvement In cooperation with ISC and Netnod, root DNS\nservers F.ROOT and I.ROOT were commissioned\non the Company\U2019s data network in Pavlodar. This\nsignificantly enhances DNS reliability, reduces latency,\nand improves network security for millions of users\nin the region. The development of DNS infrastructure\ncontributes to the resilience of the global Internet\nsystem by providing more stable connectivity for users\nin Central Asia.\nThis project is part of Kazakhtelecom JSC\U2019s broader\neffort to strengthen the region\U2019s digital infrastructure.\nThe local deployment of additional root DNS servers\naccelerates query processing and reduces DNS\nresponse times.\n5G Project\nIn 2024, Tele2 and Kcell successfully deployed 5G base\nstations in 20 cities across the Republic of Kazakhstan,\nfully meeting and even exceeding their licensing\nobligations to the government. In addition, Kazakhtelecom\nsuccessfully implemented its plans to build a 5G MBH\n(Mobile Backhaul) network for mobile operators.\nThe total cost of the project amounted\nto KZT 536.9 billion.\n130\nConstruction of a Submarine FOCL\nacross the Caspian Sea project\nThe following activities were carried out under the\nproject in 2024:\n\U097b As part of the \U201cConstruction of the FOCL along the\n\U097b\nbottom of the Caspian Sea\U201d project, in 2024 the joint\nventure Caspinet B.V. (50% \U2014 Kazakhtelecom JSC,\n50% \U2014 Azertelecom Int. LLC) prepared tender\ndocumentation and held a tender to select an EPC\ncontractor for the design and construction of the\nsubmarine FOCL along the Caspian Sea, as well\nas a contractor for supervision services. Following the\ntender process, a contract was signed with a qualified\nEPC contractor for the design and construction\nof the submarine FOCL along the route from Aktau\n(Kazakhstan) to Sumgait (Azerbaijan). A separate\ncontract was also signed with a company responsible for\ntechnical supervision of the works.\n\U097b Simultaneously, preparations began for the construction\n\U097b\nof the required onshore infrastructure. Design and\nconstruction works are underway for the beach manhole\nand cable landing stations in the city of Aktau. These\nfacilities will serve as key nodes for integrating the\nsubmarine cable into the terrestrial networks.\n\U097b At present, the project is in the active preparatory phase\n\U097b\nfor marine operations, including seabed surveys and\nroute planning.\nThe total project cost amounted to KZT 23.0 billion.\n4. SUSTAINABLE DEVELOPMENT REPORT Development of Fixed Wireless Access (FWA) in Rural Areas\nThe subsidiary Auyl Telecom LLP is implementing pilot\nprojects to develop fixed wireless access (FWA) in rural\nareas, providing high-speed internet in locations where\nthe construction of fibre-optic communication lines\n(FOCL) or GPON networks is economically unfeasible.\nThis initiative helps reduce the digital divide and\ndeliver modern connectivity to residents of remote\nregions.\nAs part of the pilot projects, solutions based on Open\nRAN and 5G FWA have already been tested. In the\nvillage of Sarybay, the average connection speed\nincreased 85-fold \U2014 from 5 Mbps to 427 Mbps \U2014\nsignificantly improving the quality of online education,\ntelemedicine, and remote work. Thus, FWA not\nonly modernises outdated technologies (WiFi, ADSL,\nCDMA EVDO) but also becomes a key tool in bridging\nthe digital gap between urban and rural areas.\nAuyl Telecom continues to actively expand its\nFWA network, with 5G being a strategic focus\nfor the company. However, a 4G network is also\nbeing developed in parallel. A successful example\nof implementation is the village of Karatala in the\nAktobe region, where 79 out of 120 households\nhave been connected. The average connection\nspeed is 46 Mbps, and the average internet traffic\nconsumption per household over a three-week\nperiod reached 191 GB. For 10 subscribers, the data\nusage exceeded 450 GB during the same period. Testing of various network functions and technical solutions\n\U097b The technical feasibility and readiness of the\n\U097b\nhardware and software complex based on Open RAN\n5G Fronthaul for providing Internet access via fixed\nwireless access were tested. The operability of the\nOpen RAN 5G Fronthaul solution was confirmed with\nsome limitations.\n\U097b The invGUARD AS-SW software suite was\n\U097b\ntested to evaluate its capabilities in monitoring\nand analyzing network traffic statistics on the\nKazakhtelecom JSC network within the TelcoCloud\nenvironment.\n\U097b The VOLTHA GPON technology was tested in the\n\U097b\nTelcoCloud environment in the city of Konaev.\nThe main idea of this solution is disaggregation and\navoidance of vendor lock-in. In traditional GPON,\nOLT (stationary equipment), software, licenses, and\nONT (customer premises equipment) are supplied\nby a single vendor and are \U201clocked,\U201d which prevents\nconnecting ONTs from other manufacturers\nto an OLT of a different vendor or using software\nfrom other providers. The VOLTHA solution\novercomes these restrictions by allowing the\nselection of white-box OLT hardware from\none manufacturer, software and licenses from\nanother, and using the openOMCI standard\nto connect ONTs from different vendors.\n\U097b The product is not yet fully ready, but the\n\U097b\nconcept and implementation activity are already\ndelivering results. The pilot broadband project\nbased on VOLTHA is currently being implemented\nin Konaev.\n\U097b The service of providing access to cache servers\n\U097b\nfor telecom operators in Kazakhstan and Central\nAsia was tested.\n\U097b Testing has begun on an indoor solution\n\U097b\nto provide mobile Internet access using PicoCell\nin locations with poor mobile/broadband signal\nquality (e.g., shops, cafes located in basements).\nIntegrated Annual Report / 2024\n131\nInFORMAtion Security and Data\npROtection\nThe Company recognises the importance of ensuring\ninformation security and protecting its clients\U2019 data.\nKazakhtelecom JSC continues to develop a robust\ninformation security and data protection management\nsystem.\nManagement Approach\nGRI 3-3, 418-1\nThe Information Security Service reports directly\nto the Managing Director for Information Security, who\noversees information security issues at the highest level\nwithin the Company.\nThe key internal documents regulating information\nsecurity include:\n\U097b Information Security Policy;\n\U097b\n\U097b Personal Data Protection Policy\n\U097b\nof Kazakhtelecom JSC;\n\U097b Information Security Concept.\n\U097b\nThese documents are available on the Company\U2019s website\nin the \U201cSustainable Development\U201d section, under the\n\U201cInformation Security and Data Protection\U201d subsection.\nKey principles of information security management:\n\U097b compliance with legal requirements;\n\U097b\n\U097b involvement of top management in the information\n\U097b\nsecurity process;\n\U097b business orientation;\n\U097b\n\U097b process-based approach;\n\U097b\n\U097b comprehensive use of methods, tools, and means\n\U097b\nof protection;\n\U097b adherence to best practices;\n\U097b\n\U097b reasonable sufficiency;\n\U097b\n\U097b awareness and personal accountability.\n\U097b\nTo ensure information security, Kazakhtelecom JSC\napplies a systematic approach. One of the key aspects\nis round-the-clock monitoring of data throughout\ntheir entire lifecycle \U2014 from the moment they enter\nthe Company\U2019s infrastructure to their archiving or\npermanent deletion.\nCurrently, the Company applies globally recognized\nbest practices in information security. Internal systems\nare protected using solutions such as secure remote\naccess to information resources, safe internet usage,\nprivileged access management (PAM), vulnerability\nscanners, and more. The Company strives to counter\nexternal threats and implements new solutions\nand methods for handling resources, including the\ndevelopment of internal infrastructure, training\nof qualified specialists, the establishment of a Security\nOperations Center (SOC), and the adoption of the Zero\nTrust concept.\nOther important security components used\nby the Company include integration into the national\ncybersecurity system (YShDI), Internet of Things (IoT)\nsecurity, deployment of honeypots, the use of machine\nlearning, and other advanced technologies. In addition,\nregular training and awareness-raising activities\nare conducted to enhance employees\U2019 knowledge\nof information security.\n4. SUSTAINABLE DEVELOPMENT REPORT Personal Data Protection\nGRI 418-1\nThe Company has developed and implemented the\nPersonal Data Protection Policy, which sets out the core\nprinciples for processing the personal data of clients,\nsuppliers, business partners, employees, and other\nindividuals. It defines the key actions related to the\ncollection, storage, and processing of personal data,\nas well as the measures taken to protect such data.\nThis Policy serves as the fundamental document in the\nfield of personal data protection, establishing the\nobjectives, tasks, and principles the Company adheres\nto in its operations. It also provides a framework for the\ndevelopment of other related internal documents.\nKey principles of personal data protection:\n\U097b respect for constitutional rights and freedoms\n\U097b\nof individuals and citizens;\n\U097b legality of personal data protection processes;\n\U097b\n\U097b confidentiality of restricted-access personal data;\n\U097b\n\U097b engagement of the Company\U2019s management\n\U097b\nin ensuring personal data protection;\n\U097b business orientation;\n\U097b\n\U097b process-based approach;\n\U097b\n\U097b comprehensive application of tools, methods,\n\U097b\nand means of protection;\n\U097b alignment with best practices;\n\U097b\n\U097b reasonable sufficiency;\n\U097b\n\U097b awareness and personal responsibility.\n\U097b\nKey Results for the Reporting Period\nIn 2024, the Company implemented a comprehensive\nset of measures in the area of information security\nto protect corporate information systems, personal\ndata, confidential information, and data transmission\nnetworks.\nAs part of maintaining an up-to-date information\nsecurity management system, the Company approved\n16 regulatory and procedural documents.\nTo raise awareness among Kazakhtelecom employees\nregarding information security, the Company issued 7\ninformational newsletters, launched 2 digital marathons\non the Corporate University training portal covering\nrules and requirements in the area of information\nsecurity, and conducted 4 cybersecurity drills in the\nform of phishing simulations to assess employees\U2019\ncyber hygiene and response actions to suspicious\nemails.\nA comprehensive inspection was carried out across\nfacilities and server rooms housing equipment\nclassified as critical information communication\ninfrastructure (CICI), along with the structural units\nresponsible for their administration. Based on identified\nnon-conformities, recommendations were issued\nto heads of relevant departments.\nAs part of operational improvements, the Company\U2019s\nIT Division reorganized internal departments in 2024\nto launch a corporate Security Operations Center\n(SOC) and switch to 24/7 operations. The SOC\nis responsible for:\n\U097b Protecting the Company\U2019s corporate perimeter;\n\U097b\n\U097b Monitoring information security (IS) events;\n\U097b\n\U097b Responding to IS incidents;\n\U097b\n\U097b Investigating IS incidents;\n\U097b\nIntegrated Annual Report / 2024\n132\nDuring the reporting period, one hotline report was\nreceived concerning a potential personal data processing\nviolation. The investigation did not confirm any client data\nbreach. No confirmed incidents of customer data leaks\nwere recorded during the period.\n\U097b Identifying vulnerabilities in the Company\U2019s\n\U097b\ninformation systems;\n\U097b Issuing recommendations for resolving IS incidents;\n\U097b\n\U097b Monitoring the effectiveness of information\n\U097b\nprotection tools.\nIn 2024, the second phase of the Company\U2019s transition\nto the ZeroTrust model was completed. A range\nof hardware and software security tools were deployed,\nsignificantly strengthening the Company\U2019s corporate\nEmployee Awareness and Training on Information Security\ninfrastructure protection. Key results of the corporate\nSOC in 2024:\nGRI 418-1\n\U097b Approximately 3,300 DDoS attacks on customer\n\U097b\nresources were repelled (peak intensity exceeding 74\nGbps), with total malicious traffic over 1,100 Tb;\n\U097b Over 710 million malicious traffic packets were blocked;\n\U097b\n\U097b Software vulnerability scanners detected around\n\U097b\n118,000 vulnerabilities in company systems, over\n64% of which were remediated by responsible\nadministrators;\n\U097b More than 40,000 network attacks were neutralized\n\U097b\nvia protection tools, along with detection of 45,000\nviruses and blocking of over 20,000 password brute-\nforce attempts;\n\U097b The Privileged Access Management (PAM)\n\U097b\nsystem monitored more than 270 privileged\nusers (system administrators, external users, and\ncontractors) across over 120 terminal server IP\naddresses used for accessing corporate information\nsystems;\n\U097b Data Leak Prevention (DLP) systems detected over\n\U097b\n800 files containing confidential information stored\nin violation of internal security requirements;\n\U097b Around 60 honeypots (decoy systems simulating\n\U097b\nreal company assets) were deployed, which helped\ndetect more than 2,000 malicious requests within the\ncorporate network.\nThe Company conducts regular training activities for its\nemployees to uphold the core principles of information\nsecurity \U2014 confidentiality, integrity, and data availability.\nInformation security is ensured at multiple levels.\nAdministratively, every employee is required to review\nand comply with the Company\U2019s internal regulations,\nrules, and policies in the field of information\nsecurity. Technically and physically, the Company\napplies a range of hardware and software systems,\nincluding cryptographic protection tools and other\nsecurity measures.\nIn addition, specialists from the Information Security\nDivision regularly undergo various advanced training\ncourses on information security, cybersecurity, and\ninformation security risks and threats. General training\nand testing on digital hygiene are conducted for\nemployees in customer service and HR departments,\nwhere the risk of unauthorized data use is relatively high.\n5. CORPORATE GOVERNANCE REPORT Board of dIrectors\nGRI 2-9\nThe Board of Directors is the governing\nbody of the Company responsible for\ndefining its strategic direction, approving\nthe development strategy and budget,\nappointing the executive body, and\nexercising other powers.\nRolES OF bOARD\nOF DiREctORS MEMbERS\nThe activities of the Board of Directors are governed\nby the legislation of the Republic of Kazakhstan,\nas well as the Charter, the Corporate Governance\nCode, the Regulations on the Board of Directors, and\nother documents adopted by the General Meeting\nof Shareholders.\n7\nmembers\ncomprise the Board of Directors\nThe Chairman manages the Board of Directors,\norganises the work and ensures efficient operation\nof the Board of Directors, conducts its meetings and\nperforms other functions stipulated by the Charter and\nthe Regulations on the Board of Directors.\nMembers of the Board of Directors are the\nshareholders\U2019 representatives acting in the interests\nof major shareholders when the Board of Directors\nperforms its activities.\nIndependent directors of the Board of Directors\nare members of all committees, consider all issues and\naccept recommendations for the Board of Directors.\nThe Audit and Sustainability Committee consists\nexclusively of independent directors. They review\nand make decisions on financial reporting, internal\nand external audit, risk and other important areas\nof activity. In addition, independent directors also\ndecide on entering into related-party transactions due\nto their independence.\n3\nindependent directors\nin the composition of the Board of Directors\n(43% of the total composition)\nIntegrated Annual Report / 2024\nElection OF the bOARD OF GRI 2-10\nMembers of the Board of Directors are elected by the\nannual General Meeting of Shareholders and re-elected\nby the extraordinary General Meeting of Shareholders\nin case of early termination of powers of previously\nelected members of the Kazakhtelecom JSC Board\nof Directors in accordance with the procedure established\nby the legislation of the Republic of Kazakhstan, the\nCharter of Kazakhtelecom JSC and the Regulations on the\nBoard of Directors of Kazakhtelecom JSC.\nThe General Meeting of Shareholders elects the members\nof the Board of Directors based on clear and transparent\nprocedures, taking into account the competences, skills,\nachievements, business reputation and professional\nexperience of the candidates. When re-electing\nindividual members of the Board of Directors or the entire\nBoard of Directors for a new term, their contribution\nto the effectiveness of the Company\U2019s Board of Directors\nis taken into account.\nThe Chairman of the Board of Directors cannot\nsimultaneously serve as the Chairman of the Fund\U2019s\nManagement Board.\nThe Board of Directors should include individuals with\nthe knowledge, skills and experience necessary for the\nBoard of Directors to perform its functions and ensure the\ngrowth of long-term value and sustainable development\nof the organisation as well as with an impeccable business\nand personal reputation.\n138\nDiREctORS\U2019 MEMbERS\nThe criteria for selecting candidates to the Board\nof Directors:\n\U097b experience in executive positions;\n\U097b\n\U097b experience as a member of the Board of Directors;\n\U097b\n\U097b length of service;\n\U097b\n\U097b education, specialisation, including international\n\U097b\ncertificates;\n\U097b competences in areas and industries (industries may\n\U097b\nvary depending on the asset portfolio);\n\U097b business reputation;\n\U097b\n\U097b existence of a direct or potential conflict of interest\n\U097b\nif elected to the Board of Directors of the\norganisation.\nElections of members of the Board of Directors are\ncarried out by shareholders by cumulative voting using\nvoting ballots, except for cases when one candidate\nis running for one seat on the Board of Directors.\nCandidates for election to the position of a member\nof the Board of Directors may be nominated from\namong:\n\U097b Individual Shareholders.\n\U097b\n\U097b Persons proposed (recommended) for election to the\n\U097b\nBoard of Directors as shareholder representatives.\n\U097b Individuals who are not a shareholder of the Company\n\U097b\nand are not proposed (not recommended) for election\nto the Board of Directors as a representative of the\nshareholder.\n5. CORPORATE GOVERNANCE REPORT DiREctORS\U2019 InDEpenDEnce\nIn accordance with the requirements of the Law\nOn Joint Stock Companies, independent members of the\nBoard of Directors should be at least 30%. In 2024,\nthis proportion in the Kazakhtelecom JSC\U2019s Board\nof Directors was 43%.\nIndependent Director is a member of the Board\nof Directors who:\n\U097b is not an affiliate of this joint stock company and\n\U097b\nhas not been an affiliate of this joint stock company\nfor three years preceding his election to the Board\nof Directors (except for the case of his tenure\nas an independent director of this joint stock company);\n\U097b is not an affiliate of any affiliate of this joint stock\n\U097b\ncompany;\n\U097b is not a subordinate to any officials of the joint-\n\U097b\nstock company or affiliated entities of the joint-\nstock company and has not been subordinate to any\nsuch officials during the three years preceding his\nelection to the Board of Directors;\ncOnflicts OF intERESt\nGRI 2-15\nKazakhtelecom JSC has a Conflict of Interest Policy.\nThe Policy defines the procedure for prevention,\nidentification and regulation of conflict of interests,\nprocedures for interaction and coordination\nof the Company\U2019s bodies and/or persons in case\nof occurrence or probability of occurrence of conflict\nof interests.\nIntegrated Annual Report / 2024\n143\n\U097b is not a government official;\n\U097b\n\U097b is not a shareholder\U2019s representative at meetings\n\U097b\nof the bodies of the joint stock company and has\nnot been such a representative during the three\nyears preceding his election to the Board of Direc-\ntors;\n\U097b does not participate in the audit of this joint stock\n\U097b\ncompany as an auditor working as part of an audit\norganisation and has not participated in such an au-\ndit during the three years preceding his election\nto the Board of Directors.\nThe independent directors of the Company\U2019s Board\nof Directors fully met the independence criteria\nin 2024. For more details, please refer to the\ndocument titled \U201cDeclaration of Independence of the\nBoard of Directors\U201d available on the Company\U2019s\nwebsite. https://sustainability.telecom.kz/?page_id=73\nIn 2024, the Board of Directors recorded no conflicts\nof interest in its work.\n5. CORPORATE GOVERNANCE REPORT Management\nBoard\nThe Management Board is the collective executive\nbody of the Company. It acts on behalf of the Company,\nincluding representing its interests and entering into\ntransactions in accordance with the legislation of the\nRepublic of Kazakhstan and the Company\U2019s Charter.\nThe Management Board approves the staffing of the\nCompany, excluding the employees of the Central\nOffice, and makes decisions that are mandatory for all\nemployees of the Company.\nThe Management Board is responsible for overseeing\nthe current operations of Kazakhtelecom JSC and\nis authorised to make decisions on any matters\nnot reserved by the legislation of the Republic\nof Kazakhstan or the Company\U2019s Charter to other\ngoverning bodies or officials.\nThe Management Board consists of seven members,\nincluding the Chairperson of the Management Board\nand other 2024\nREMunERAtion OF the bOARD\nGRI 2-19, 2-20, 2-21\nThe terms and procedure for the payment of remuneration\nto the Company\U2019s senior executives for the reporting\nperiod are governed by the Rules for the Payment\nof Performance-Based Remuneration to Senior Executives\nof Kazakhtelecom JSC, approved by the decision of the\nBoard of Directors dated 14 February 2023 (Minutes No. 2)\n(the \U201cRules\U201d).\nKey principles of the Rules include:\n\U097b the link between remuneration and the achievement\n\U097b\nof objectives that serve the interests of the Company\nand its shareholders;\n\U097b simplicity and transparency in determining the amount\n\U097b\nof remuneration;\n\U097b dependence of remuneration on both the Company\U2019s\n\U097b\nperformance and the employee\U2019s individual\neffectiveness.\nKey Performance Indicators (KPIs) are used to assess the\nperformance of senior executives.\nThe performance evaluation procedure for senior\nexecutives consists of the following stages:\n\U097b setting KPIs and their target values;\n\U097b\n\U097b approval of KPIs;\n\U097b\n\U097b monitoring of performance;\n\U097b\n\U097b calculation and approval of actual performance\n\U097b\nresults.\nPerformance-based remuneration for the reporting period\nis paid within the funds allocated for this purpose in the\nCompany\U2019s budget, following the formal approval of the\nfinancial and economic performance results based on the\naudited financial statements for the reporting period.\nThe maximum amount of performance-based\nremuneration is determined in accordance with the\nestablished remuneration structure.\nThe total amount of salaries and all types of monetary\nincentives paid to the members of the Management Board\nin 2024 amounted to KZT 634,562 thousand, net of taxes.\n152\nInFORMAtion\ntRAnspAREncy\nAs a public company, the largest player in Kazakhstan\U2019s\ntelecommunications market, and a portfolio company\nof Samruk-Kazyna JSC, Kazakhtelecom JSC places\nthe utmost importance on openness, transparency, and\naccountability. The Company builds communication with\nall key stakeholder audiences\U2014including shareholders,\ninvestors, clients (both external and internal), government\nauthorities of the Republic of Kazakhstan, the media,\npublic associations, bloggers, and other interested\nparties\U2014on the basis of its officially adopted and\neffective Information Policy (available at: https://telecom.\nkz/ru/pages/12089/171752).\nThe Company\U2019s Information Policy is guided by the\nfollowing principles:\n\U097b Reliability;\n\U097b\n\U097b Timeliness;\n\U097b\n\U097b Accessibility;\n\U097b\n\U097b Completeness;\n\U097b\n\U097b Independence;\n\U097b\n\U097b Regularity;\n\U097b\n\U097b Systematic approach;\n\U097b\n\U097b Proactivity;\n\U097b\n\U097b Multimedia engagement.\n\U097b\nThe purpose of the Information Policy is to foster\na positive perception of the Company among information\nrecipients, build long-term and loyal relationships with\nstakeholders, enhance the Company\U2019s information\ntransparency, and establish a clear and consistent\ninformation flow between the Company and its target\naudiences.\nAccording to data from the Youscan media monitoring\nsystem, the total number of mentions of the Company,\nits products, projects, services, and offerings in various\ndomestic, foreign, national, and regional media outlets\namounted to 13,462 in 2024.\n5. CORPORATE GOVERNANCE REPORT Corporate ethICs GRI 2-23\nCorporate ethics issues\nin Kazakhtelecom JSC are governed\nby the Code of Business Conduct\nand the Corporate Governance Code.\nThe Code of Business Conduct and the\nCorporate Governance Code are public\ndocuments and are freely distributed\nby the Company to employees,\nshareholders, customers, partners, and\nother stakeholders.\nThe Code of Business Ethics of Kazakhtelecom JSC\nwas developed in accordance with the legislation of the\nRepublic of Kazakhstan and takes into account the\nrequirements of the International Labour Organization,\nas well as the Company\U2019s Charter, Corporate\nGovernance Code, and a number of other internal\ndocuments of Kazakhtelecom JSC.\nThe provisions of the Code of Business Ethics and the\nCorporate Governance Code are mandatory for all\nemployees and officers of the Company.\nAll officers and employees are required to confirm\nin writing that they have read and understood the Code\nof Business Ethics. In addition, the Company regularly\nconducts training sessions for officers and employees\nto ensure awareness of the Code of Business Ethics,\nthe role of the Ombudsperson, and the availability of the\nwhistleblowing system for reporting suspected violations.\nIn 2024, a total of 12,104 employees of the Company\ncompleted training on the Code of Business Ethics.\nThe Company\U2019s key principles of business ethics include:\n\U097b Compliance with legal requirements;\n\U097b\n\U097b Fairness;\n\U097b\n\U097b Integrity;\n\U097b\n\U097b Transparency;\n\U097b\n\U097b Accountability;\n\U097b\n\U097b Competence and professionalism;\n\U097b\n\U097b Trust;\n\U097b\n\U097b Meritocracy.\n\U097b\nThe Ombudsperson is responsible for ensuring adherence\nto ethical principles and resolving social and labor-related\nconflicts. The Ombudsperson is an employee of the\nCompany appointed by the Board of Directors to support\nconflict prevention and resolution in labor relations,\nprotect the rights and legitimate interests of employees,\npromote corporate values, and uphold the principles\nof business ethics.\nThe Code of Business Conduct of Kazakhtelecom JSC is available on the Company\U2019s website telecom.kz.\nIntegrated Annual Report / 2024\n153\nrIsk Management\nand Internal\nControls\nThe Corporate Risk Management\nand Internal Control System\n(CRMS and IC) is aimed at providing\nreasonable assurance of achieving\nthe goals set by the governing body\nof Kazakhtelecom JSC.\nIn today\U2019s environment, emerging risks in the\ntelecommunications sector include cybersecurity\nthreats, changes in legislation and regulatory\nframeworks, as well as technological challenges\nsuch as the deployment of 5G and the Internet\nof Things (IoT). The increasing number of cyberattacks\non communication networks poses risks of confidential\ndata breaches, service disruptions, and significant\nimplications for both business operations and society\nat large.\nAs the largest telecommunications operator\nin Kazakhstan, Kazakhtelecom JSC plays a key role\nin advancing telecommunications infrastructure and\nensuring the security of communications across\nthe country. The Company actively adopts modern\ntechnologies and strives to enhance the cybersecurity\nof its networks to protect customer data and ensure\nthe uninterrupted delivery of communication services.\nThese efforts are supported by the functioning of the\nCorporate Risk Management and Internal Control System\nCRMS and IC) at Kazakhtelecom JSC, which is designed\nto safeguard assets, improve business processes,\nenhance operational efficiency, and ensure compliance\nwith applicable legal requirements.\nThe timely identification of non-conformities and\ninefficiencies, the analysis and forecasting of potential\nscenarios, and the development of preventive\nand mitigating measures make a significant contribution\nto the achievement of the Company\U2019s operational and\nstrategic objectives.\n5. control\npractices, including the Committee of Sponsoring\nOrganizations of the Treadway Commission (COSO),\nTMForum, and ISO standards. The system is based on the\n\U201cthree lines of defense\U201d model.\nThe Company recognises that risk management is effective only when every employee is in the process. Therefore, we are\nconstantly developing a risk-oriented culture with the following key aspects: Tone on top The Company\U2019s management sets an example for employees in discussing, identifying and assessing risks, and is actively\ninvolved in risk management.\nResponsibility for the system\U2019s operation is allocated in line with this model as follows:\nfIrst line of defense\nManagement (process owners) bear primary responsibility for managing risks associated with day-to-day operations.\nThis line is also responsible for developing, implementing, and operating control mechanisms and monitoring their\nperformance.\nCultural spectrumSecond line of defense\nTimely provision of risk information is encouraged. Acceptance of risks is allowed if they are not critical but may\ncontribute to business development. The risks themselves are viewed not only as a potentially negative event, but also\nas an opportunity to improve the Company\U2019s processes.\nIdentifies emerging risks in the Company\U2019s daily operations and ensures compliance with regulatory requirements and\ninternal policies. It develops supporting policies, documentation, tools, and technologies.\nInvolvementThird line of defense\nRisk management training is organised for employees, accessible guidance materials are developed, and communication\nand support channels are organised.\nAssesses the effectiveness of the internal control system (ICS), reports to the Management Board and the Audit\nCommittee, and provides audit assurance to regulators and external auditors, demonstrating the effectiveness of the\ncontrol environment and framework.\n5. APPENDICES Integrated Annual Report / 2024\n168\nDeclaration on the Independence\nof the Board of dIrectors\nBalance of sKIlls, eXperience,\nand Knowledge:\nThe Board of Directors and its committees must maintain\na balance of skills, experience, and knowledge to ensure\nindependent, objective, and effective decision-making\nin the interests of the organization, while upholding\nfair treatment of all shareholders and the principles\nof sustainable development.\nIndependent dIrectors: The Board of Directors must include a sufficient number\nof independent directors to ensure the independence\nof decisions and fair treatment of all shareholders.\nThe recommended proportion of independent directors\nis up to fifty percent of the total number of members\nof the Board of Directors.\ndIversity of the Board\nof dIrectors:\nThe composition of the Board of Directors must reflect\ndiversity in the following areas:\n\U097b Experience;\n\U097b\n\U097b Personal characteristics;\n\U097b\n\U097b National, ethnic, and cultural background;\n\U097b\n\U097b Gender composition.\n\U097b\nRequirements for Independent\ndIrectors:\nThe requirements for independent directors are defined\nin accordance with the legislation of the Republic\nof Kazakhstan and the Charter of Kazakhtelecom JSC\n(hereinafter \U2014 the Company).\nCircumstances Affecting\ndIrector Independence:\nA director cannot have been an employee of the\nCompany or its subsidiaries/affiliates within the last\nthree years. A director or a member of their immediate\nfamily must not have received any compensation from\nthe Company or its subsidiaries/affiliates during the\ncurrent fiscal year, except for remuneration for serving\non the Board of Directors. Immediate family members\nof a director must not hold executive positions in the\nCompany or its subsidiaries/affiliates. A director must\nnot act as a consultant to, or representative of, any\nentity providing consulting services to the Company\nand/or its management. A director must not be\naffiliated with major customers or suppliers of the\nCompany. A director must not be affiliated with non-\nprofit organizations receiving significant donations from\nthe Company. A director must not have served as the\nCompany\U2019s auditor during the three years preceding their\nappointment to the Board of Directors.\nDuties of an Independent\ndIrector:\nAn independent director must monitor any potential\nloss of independent status and provide early written\nnotice to the Chair of the Board of Directors in the event\nof such situations. If circumstances arise that affect the\nindependence of a member of the Board of Directors, the\nChair of the Board must promptly notify the shareholders\nto allow for an appropriate decision to be made.\n6. APPENDICES Integrated Annual Report / 2024\n170\nReport on Compliance with the PrinCIples\nand Provisions of the Corporate Gover-\nnance Code of Kazakhtelecom JSC for 2024\nThis Report has been prepared in accordance with\nparagraph 15, chapter 5 of the Corporate Governance\nCode of Kazakhtelecom JSC \U201cEffectiveness of the\nBoard of Directors and the Executive Body\U201d.\nThe activities of Kazakhtelecom JSC and its corporate\npractices demonstrate full compliance with the\nprinciples and provisions of the Corporate Governance\nCode.\ncORpORAte GovERnance pRinciplES OF the Joint-Stock cOMpany\n\U201cSovEREign wEAlth Fund SAMRuk-KAZyna\U201d\nChapter 1. Government as a Shareholder of the Fund Chapter 2. Interaction Between\nthe Fund and Organizations.\nRole of the Fund as a National\nManaging Holding\nAlthough this chapter is titled as such, it contains\nprovisions that the Company is expected to follow\nin its operations. In particular, it is stated that the main\nstrategic objective of the Fund\U2019s organizations is the\ngrowth of long-term value and sustainable development.\nAll decisions and actions must be aligned with the\ndevelopment strategy.\nThe Company\U2019s governing bodies are fully independent\nand autonomous in making decisions and performing\nactions within their competence. Relations between\nshareholders and the Company are managed through\nthe Board of Directors in accordance with the principles\nof sound corporate governance.\nDisclosure of information on the Company\U2019s activities\nis carried out in accordance with the Law \U201cOn Joint-Stock\nCompanies\U201d and the Company\U2019s Charter via placement\nof required information in the mass media (including\nthe financial reporting depository and stock exchange\nwebsites). Upon request, certain information is also\nprovided to shareholders directly.\nThe Company has an Internal Audit Service, a Compliance\nService, and the roles of Corporate Secretary and\nOmbudsperson, all of which operate in accordance with\napplicable legislation and the internal regulations of the\nCompany. These functions are elaborated in detail below\nin this Report.\nThe corporate governance system is a set of processes that\nensure the management and oversight of the Company\U2019s\nactivities, as well as the relationships between the Management\nBoard, Board of Directors, shareholders, and stakeholders.\nThese matters are clearly regulated in the Charter, and the\nprovisions on the General Meeting of Shareholders, Board\nof Directors, Management Board, and other internal documents.\nSamruk-Kazyna JSC (hereinafter \U2014 the Fund) participates\nin company management through its role as a major shareholder\nand through the Board of Directors.\nThe Board of Directors of the Company is fully autonomous\nin making decisions within its competence. The Fund\U2019s position\non certain issues is communicated through its representatives\non the Board of Directors.\nThe Company is managed by its governing bodies in accordance\nwith the law and its Charter.\n6. APPENDICES Chapter 3. Sustainable\nDevelopment\nThe Corporate Governance and Sustainable\nDevelopment Department coordinates\nsustainability activities. Improving the sustainable\ndevelopment management system is an integral part\nof Kazakhtelecom JSC\U2019s Strategy through 2032.\nIn 2024, the Company developed and approved an ESG\nStrategy (Minutes No. 15 dated 19.09.2024), which is part\nof the broader JRun business strategy and considers the\nCompany\U2019s role in implementing government programs\nin the areas of IT, education, infrastructure, and low-\ncarbon development. It contributes to the effective\nachievement of financial stability and competitiveness.\nUnder the ESG Strategy, the Company plans to enhance\nits corporate climate risk management system.\nIn 2024, the Company identified climate-related\nrisks and opportunities in accordance with the TCFD\nRecommendations and developed a methodological\napproach for their identification; conducted climate\nscenario analysis in line with TCFD recommendations;\nand developed an adaptation plan to address identified\nphysical climate risks.\nKazakhtelecom JSC places great emphasis on ESG\ndevelopment. In February 2023, the Board of Directors\napproved the ESG Practices Development Roadmap\nof Kazakhtelecom JSC, comprising 108 actions in the\nareas of environment, social balance, and corporate\ngovernance. In 2024, the Company implemented the\nfollowing measures under this Roadmap:\n\U097b disclosure of climate-related information;\n\U097b\n\U097b obtained an independent ESG rating from S&P Global;\n\U097b\n\U097b assessed the current level of biodiversity in its\n\U097b\noperational areas.\nIn 2024, the Company continued implementing measures\nto reduce greenhouse gas emissions in line with its Low-\nCarbon Development Program for 2022\U20132032, approved\nby the Board of Directors.\nChapter 4. Shareholder rIghts and\nFair Treatment\nThe protection of shareholder rights is a key\ncommitment of the Company. Kazakhtelecom JSC\nstrictly adheres to the shareholder rights stipulated\nin legislation and internal regulations and ensures\nfair treatment of shareholders. Shareholders are\npromptly informed about relevant events such\nas general meetings, decisions taken, and other matters.\nThe Company also promptly provides requested\ninformation to shareholders.\nIntegrated Annual Report / 2024\nChapter 5. Effectiveness\nof the Board of dIrectors and the\neXecutive Body\nThe Board of Directors, accountable to the General\nMeeting of Shareholders, provides strategic leadership\nand oversight of the Management Board\U2019s activities.\nThe Management Board, accountable to the Board\nof Directors, manages the day-to-day operations and\nensures alignment with the strategy, development\nplan, and decisions made by the Board and the General\nMeeting of Shareholders.\nThe powers of the Board of Directors and the\nManagement Board are clearly defined and delineated.\nThe Board of Directors and its committees maintain\na balance of skills, experience, and knowledge to ensure\nindependent, objective, and effective decision-making\nin the Company\U2019s interests, fair shareholder treatment,\nand sustainable development.\nThe Board includes experts from various fields\n(telecommunications, finance, marketing, technology,\netc.) with broad, including international, experience.\nThe number of independent directors complies with and\nexceeds the legal requirement (at least 30%).\n171\nThe election of the Board of Directors is conducted\nstrictly in accordance with the procedures set\nby legislation and the Company\U2019s Charter. The election\nprocedure, term of office, and the Board\U2019s activities are\ngoverned by internal regulations. An induction program\nis in place for newly elected Board members.\nThe Chairperson of the Board of Directors is responsible\nfor overall leadership, ensuring the effective functioning\nof the Board, and facilitating constructive dialogue\namong Board members, major shareholders, and the\nManagement Board.\nThe roles and responsibilities of the Chairperson and\nCEO are clearly separated and stipulated in the Charter\nand internal regulations.\nThe Board committees contribute to in-depth and thorough\nconsideration of issues within the Board\U2019s competence and\nimprove decision quality, particularly in the areas of audit,\nrisk management, strategy, HR, and social matters.\nIn 2024, three committees operated actively and\neffectively: the Audit and Sustainable Development\nCommittee, the HR, Remuneration and Social Matters\nCommittee, and the Strategic Planning Committee. Their\nroles are clearly defined in the regulations, they review\na broad range of issues, and provide recommendations\nto the Board. The outcomes of their work are regularly\nreviewed and positively assessed by the Board.\n6. APPENDICES The preparation and conduct of Board meetings are\naimed at maximizing effectiveness. The recommendation to appoint the\nexecutive body for up to three years is observed.\nKPIs for the CEO and executive team are approved\nannually by the Board.\nIn case of corporate conflicts, the parties seek resolution\nthrough negotiation to ensure the effective protection\nof the organization\U2019s and stakeholders\U2019 interests. No\ncorporate conflicts occurred in 2024, as in previous years.\nTo ensure adherence to business ethics and effective\nresolution of socio-labour disputes, the Company\nhas appointed an Ombudsperson.
