MATERIAL ACCOUNTING POLICIES (continued)\nIncome tax\nCurrent income tax\nCurrent income tax assets and liabilities are measured at the amount expected to be recovered from or paid to the\ntaxation authorities. The tax rates and tax laws used to compute the amount are those that are enacted or substantively\nenacted at the reporting date in the countries where the Group operates and generates taxable profit.\nCurrent income tax relating to items recognised directly in equity is recognised in equity and not in the consolidated\nstatement of comprehensive income. Management periodically evaluates positions taken in the tax returns with respect\nto situations in which applicable tax regulations are subject to interpretation and establishes provisions where\nappropriate.\nDeferred tax\nDeferred tax is provided using the liability method on temporary differences between the tax bases of assets and\nliabilities and their carrying amounts for financial reporting purposes at the reporting date.\nDeferred tax liabilities are recognised for all taxable temporary differences, except:\nWhen the deferred tax liability arises from the initial recognition of goodwill or an asset or liability in a\ntransaction that is not a business combination and, at the time of the transaction, affects neither the accounting\nprofit nor taxable profit or loss;\nIn respect of taxable temporary differences associated with investments in subsidiaries, associates and interests\nin joint arrangements, when the timing of the reversal of the temporary differences can be controlled and it is\nprobable that the temporary differences will not reverse in the foreseeable future\nDeferred tax assets are recognised for all deductible temporary differences, the carry forward of unused tax credits and\nany unused tax losses. Deferred tax assets are recognised to the extent that it is probable that taxable profit will be\navailable against which the deductible temporary differences and the carry forward of unused tax credits and unused tax\nlosses can be utilised, except:\nWhen the deferred tax asset relating to the deductible temporary difference arises from the initial recognition of\nan asset or liability in a transaction that is not a business combination and, at the time of the transaction, affects\nneither the accounting profit nor taxable profit or loss;\nIn respect of deductible temporary differences associated with investments in subsidiaries, associates and\ninterests in joint arrangements, deferred tax assets are recognised only to the extent that it is probable that the\ntemporary differences will reverse in the foreseeable future and taxable profit will be available against which the\ntemporary differences can be utilised.\nThe carrying amount of deferred tax assets is reviewed at each reporting date and reduced to the extent that it is no\nlonger probable that sufficient taxable profit will be available to allow all or part of the deferred tax assets to be utilised.\nUnrecognised deferred tax assets are re-assessed at each reporting date and are recognised to the extent that it has\nbecome probable that future taxable profits will allow the deferred tax asset to be recovered.\nDeferred tax assets and liabilities are measured at the tax rates that are expected to apply to the reporting year when the\nasset is realised or the liability is settled, based on tax rates (and tax laws) that have been enacted or substantively\nenacted as at the reporting date.\nDeferred tax relating to items recognised outside profit or loss is recognised outside profit or loss. Deferred tax items\nare recognised in correlation to the underlying transaction either in OCI or directly in equity.\nTax benefits acquired as part of a business combination, but not satisfying the criteria for separate recognition at that\ndate, are recognised subsequently to reflect new information about facts and circumstances change. The adjustment is\neither treated as a reduction in goodwill (as long as it does not exceed goodwill) if it was incurred during the\nmeasurement period or recognised in profit or loss.\nThe Group offsets deferred tax assets and deferred tax liabilities if and only if it has a legally enforceable right to set off\ncurrent tax assets and current tax liabilities and the deferred tax assets and deferred tax liabilities relate to income taxes\nlevied by the same taxation authority on either the same taxable entity or different taxable entities which intend either to\nsettle current tax liabilities and assets on a net basis, or to realise the assets and settle the liabilities simultaneously, in\neach future period in which significant amounts of deferred tax liabilities or assets are expected to be settled or\nrecovered.\n27\nIntegrated Annual Report / 2024\nKazakhtelecom JSC NOTES TO THE CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS (continued)\nConsolidated financial statements\n3. MATERIAL ACCOUNTING POLICIES (continued)\nContingent assets and liabilities\nContingent assets are not recognised in the consolidated financial statements. Where an inflow of economic benefits is\nprobable, they are disclosed.\nContingent liabilities are not recognised in the consolidated financial statements unless an outflow of resources\nembodying economic benefits has become probable. They are disclosed unless the possibility of an outflow of resources\nembodying economic benefits is remote.\nRelated parties\nIn accordance with IAS 24 Related Party Disclosures, parties are considered to be related if one party has the ability to\ncontrol the other party or exercise significant influence over the other party in making financial or operational decisions.\nTransactions with related parties are used to reflect the status of settlements for property, work and services received\nfrom companies or sold to companies that are related parties to the Group. Items of a similar nature are disclosed in\naggregate except when separate disclosure is necessary for an understanding of the effects of related party transactions\non the consolidated financial statements.\n4. CRITICAL ACCOUNTING JUDGEMENTS, ESTIMATES AND ASSUMPTIONS\nThe preparation of the Group's consolidated financial statements requires the management to make judgements,\nestimates and assumptions that affect the reported amounts of revenues, expenses, assets and liabilities, and the\naccompanying disclosures, and the disclosure of contingent liabilities in the consolidated financial statements.\nUncertainty about these assumptions and estimates could result in outcomes that require a material adjustment to the\ncarrying amount of assets or liabilities affected in future periods.\nOther disclosures relating to the Group\U2019s exposure to risks and uncertainties includes:\nFinancial instruments and financial risk management objectives and principles \U2013 Note 45;\nSensitivity analyses disclosures \U2013 Notes 11 and 24.\nJudgements\nIn the process of applying the Group\U2019s accounting policies, management has made the following judgements, which\nhave the most significant effect on the amounts recognised in the consolidated financial statements:\nDetermining the lease term of contracts with renewal and termination options \U2013 the Group as a lessee\nThe Group determines the lease term as the non-cancellable term of the lease, together with any periods covered by an\noption to extend the lease if it is reasonably certain to be exercised, or any periods covered by an option to terminate the\nlease, if it is reasonably certain not to be exercised.\nThe Group has several lease contracts that include extension and termination options. The Group applies judgement in\nevaluating whether it is reasonably certain whether or not to exercise the option to renew or terminate the lease. That is,\nit considers all relevant factors that create an economic incentive for it to exercise either the renewal or termination.\nAfter the commencement date, the Group re-assesses the lease term if there is a significant event or change in\ncircumstances that is within its control and affects its ability to exercise or not to exercise the option to renew or to\nterminate.\nThe Group included the renewal period as part of the lease term for leases of machinery and equipment with a shorter\nnon-cancellable period. The Group typically exercises its option to renew for these leases because there will be\na significant negative effect on production if a replacement asset is not readily available.\n28\n184\nKazakhtelecom JSC Consolidated financial statements\nNOTES TO THE CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS (continued)\n4. CRITICAL Judgements (continued)\nACCOUNTING JUDGEMENTS, ESTIMATES AND ASSUMPTIONS (continued)\nThe Group cannot readily determine the interest rate implicit in the lease; therefore, it uses its incremental borrowing\nrate (IBR) to measure lease liabilities. The IBR is the rate of interest that the Group would have to pay to borrow over a\nsimilar term, and with a similar security, the funds necessary to obtain an asset of a similar value to the right-of-use\nasset in a similar economic environment. The IBR therefore reflects what the Group \U2018would have to pay\U2019, which\nrequires estimation when no observable rates are available (such as for subsidiaries that do not enter into financing\ntransactions) or when they need to be adjusted to reflect the terms and conditions of the lease (for example, when leases\nare not in the subsidiary\U2019s functional currency). The Group estimates the IBR using observable inputs (such as market\ninterest rates) when available and is required to make certain entity-specific estimates (such as the subsidiary\U2019s stand-\nalone credit rating).\nUseful lives of property and equipment and intangible assets\nThe Group assesses the remaining useful lives of items of property and equipment and intangible assets at least at each\nfinancial year-end and, if expectations differ from previous estimates, the changes are accounted for as a change in an\naccounting estimate in accordance with IAS 8 Accounting Policies, Changes in Accounting Estimates and Errors.\nOn initial recognition, the Group assessed the useful life of 5G frequencies to be 15 years based on an assessment of the\ndevelopment of communication technologies, the practices of other mobile operators and the expected average period of\nincome generation from the use of 5G frequencies. As at 31 December 2024, the Group concluded that the useful life of\n5G frequencies remained unchanged.\nEstimates and assumptions\nThe key assumptions concerning the future and other key sources of estimation uncertainty at the reporting date that\nhave a significant risk of causing a material adjustment to the carrying amounts of assets and liabilities within the next\nfinancial year are described below. The Group based its assumptions and estimates on parameters available at the time\nwhen the consolidated financial statements were prepared. Existing circumstances and assumptions about future\ndevelopments, however, may change due to market changes or circumstances arising that are beyond the Group\U2019s\ncontrol. Such changes are reflected in the assumptions when they occur.\nImpairment of non-financial assets\nImpairment exists when the carrying amount of an asset or a cash generating unit exceeds its recoverable amount, which\nis the higher of its fair value less costs of disposal and its value in use. The fair value less costs to sell calculation is\nbased on available data from binding sales transactions in an arm\U2019s length transaction of similar assets or observable\nmarket prices less incremental costs for disposing of the asset. The value in use calculation is based on a discounted\ncash flow model. The cash flows are derived from the budget for the next 5 (five) years and do not include restructuring\nactivities that the Group is not yet committed to or significant future investments that will enhance the asset\U2019s\nperformance of the cash generating unit being tested. The recoverable amount is most sensitive to the discount rate used\nfor the discounted cash flow model as well as the expected future cash inflows and growth rates used for extrapolation\npurposes. The key assumptions used to determine the recoverable amount for the different CGUs, including a sensitivity\nanalysis, are disclosed and further explained in Note 11.\nAllowance for expected credit losses\nThe Group recognises a provision for expected credit losses for receivables and funds in credit institutions (cash and\ncash equivalents, and bank deposits).For trade and other receivables, the Group has applied the simplified approach\npermitted by the standard and has calculated expected credit losses based on the lifetime of these financial instruments.\nThe Group used a provision model that is prepared based on the Group\U2019s historical credit loss experience, adjusted for\nthe factors specific to the debtors and the economic environment. The Group will calibrate the matrix to adjust the\nhistorical credit loss experience with forward-looking information.\nFor instance, if forecast economic conditions (i.e., gross domestic product) are expected to deteriorate over the next year\nwhich can lead to an increased number of defaults in the telecommunications sector, the historical default rates are\nadjusted. At every reporting date, the historical observed default rates are updated and changes in the forward-looking\nestimates are analysed.\n29\n6. CRITICAL ACCOUNTING JUDGEMENTS, ESTIMATES AND ASSUMPTIONS (continued)\nEstimates and assumptions (continued)\nAllowance for expected credit losses (continued)\nThe assessment of the correlation between historical observed default rates, forecast economic conditions and ECLs is a\nsignificant estimate. The amount of ECLs is sensitive to changes in circumstances and in forecast economic conditions.\nAlso, the Group\U2019s historical credit loss experience and forecast economic conditions may not be representative of the\ncustomer\U2019s actual default in the future. The information about the ECLs on the Group\U2019s trade receivables is disclosed in\nNote 15.\nFor funds in credit institutions (cash and cash equivalents, bank deposits), the Group calculated expected credit losses\nbased on the 12-month period. The 12-month expected credit losses is the portion of lifetime expected credit losses that\nresults from default events on a financial instrument that are possible within 12 months after the reporting date.\nHowever, when there has been a significant increase in credit risk since origination, the provision will be based on the\nlifetime expected credit losses.\nThe Group considers that there has been a significant increase in credit risk when contractual payments are more than\n30 days past due. Also, it is considered that a financial asset is in default when contractual payments are 90 days past\ndue. However, in certain cases, the Group may also consider a financial asset to be in default when internal or external\ninformation indicates that the Group is unlikely to receive the outstanding contractual amounts in full before taking into\naccount any credit enhancements held by the Group.\nThus, as at 31 December 2024, the provision for expected credit losses was created in the amount of\nKZT 19,549,197 thousand (2023: KZT 17,628,662 thousand) (Notes 12, 15, 17 and 20). Changes in the economy,\nindustry or specific customer conditions would have an impact on these allowances recorded in the consolidated\nfinancial statements.\nSignificant financing component\nThe Group concludes that certain long-term contracts contain significant financing components due to the time interval\nbetween the provision of the Group\U2019s services to the customer and the moment the customer pays for such services.\nThe transaction price for such contracts is discounted, using the rate that would be reflected in a separate financing\ntransaction between the Group and its customers at contract inception.\nCost to obtain a contract\nThe Group considers commission to sales agents to be an additional cost to obtain a contract, and capitalises such costs\nto obtain contracts with customers as an asset. The Group depreciates the costs to obtain a contract with customers on a\nsystematic basis, which corresponds to the timing of the provision of services to customers. The Group reviews\ndepreciation periods if the expected service dates have changed.\nContract liabilities\nDeferred revenues are recognised as contract liabilities and recorded over the expected period of the customer\nrelationship. In making its judgements, management considered the detailed criteria for the recognition of revenues\nfrom contracts with customers set out in IFRS 15, industry practice and the Group\U2019s historical churn rate.\nNon-refundable upfront fees\nUpfront fees received for activation and connection to the fixed line and the wireless network that do not represent a\nseparate earning process are recognised as contract liabilities and recorded over the expected period of the customer\nrelationship. In making its judgements, management considered the detailed criteria for the recognition of revenues\nfrom connection fees set out in IAS 15, industry practice and the Company\U2019s historical churn rate. As at\n31 December 2024, average customer relationship period is assessed as 13 (thirteen) years for fixed line customers and\n5 (five) years for internet customers.\n30\nIntegrated Annual Report / 2024\nKazakhtelecom JSC NOTES TO THE CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS (continued)\nConsolidated financial statements\n4. CRITICAL ACCOUNTING JUDGEMENTS, ESTIMATES AND ASSUMPTIONS (continued)\nEstimates and assumptions (continued)\nDecommissioning liability\nDecommissioning liabilities are recognised in respect of the estimated future costs of closure and restoration and for\nenvironmental rehabilitation costs in the reporting period when the related environmental disturbance occurs.\nDecommissioning costs are recorded at the discounted value of expected liability settlement costs calculated using\nestimated cash flows and recognised as part of the initial cost of the particular asset. The cash flows are discounted at a\ncurrent pre-tax rate, which reflects the risks inherent in the decommissioning liability. The unwinding of the discount is\nexpensed as incurred and recognised in the consolidated statement of comprehensive income as finance costs. The\nestimated future costs of decommissioning are reviewed annually and adjusted as appropriate. Changes in the estimated\nfuture costs, or in the discount rate applied, are added to or deducted from the cost of the asset.\nEmployee benefit obligations\nThe Group uses the actuarial valuation method for measurement of the present value of defined employee benefit\nobligation and related current service cost. This involves the use of demographic assumptions about the future\ncharacteristics of current and former employees who are eligible for benefits (mortality, both during and after\nemployment, rates of employee turnover, etc.) as well as financial assumptions (discount rate, future salary increases).\nDue to the long term nature of these benefits, such estimates are subject to significant uncertainty.\nThe current portion of employee benefit obligations represents the obligations which the Group is going to repay within\nthe twelve months period since the end of the annual reporting period.\nIn determining the appropriate discount rate, the Group\U2019s management considers the interest rates of high-yield\ncorporate bonds in respective currencies.\nThe mortality rate is based on publicly available mortality tables. Future salary increases and pension increases are\nbased on expected future inflation rates.\nFurther details about the assumptions used are contained in Note 24.\nTaxes\nDeferred tax assets are recognised for unused tax losses to the extent that it is probable that taxable profit will be\navailable against which the losses can be utilised. Significant management judgement is required to determine the\namount of deferred tax assets that can be recognised in the consolidated financial statements, based upon the likely\ntiming and the level of future taxable profits, together with future tax planning strategies.\nAs at 31 December 2024, the carrying amount of recognised tax assets was KZT 163,330 thousand (31 December 2023:\nKZT 369,451 thousand). Further details are contained in Note 40.\nLeases \U2013 estimating the incremental borrowing rate\nThe Group cannot readily determine the interest rate implicit in the lease; therefore, it uses its incremental borrowing\nrate (IBR) to measure lease liabilities. The IBR is the rate of interest that the Group would have to pay to borrow over a\nsimilar term, and with a similar security, the funds necessary to obtain an asset of a similar value to the right-of-use\nasset in a similar economic environment. Therefore, the IBR reflects what the Group \U2018would have to pay\U2019, which\nrequires estimation when no observable rates are available or when they need to be adjusted to reflect the terms and\nconditions of the lease. The Group estimates the IBR using observable inputs (such as market interest rates) when\navailable and is required to make certain entity-specific estimates.\nFair value measurement of financial instruments\nWhen the fair value of financial instruments and financial liabilities recorded in the consolidated statement of financial\nposition cannot be measured based on data in active markets, their fair value is measured using valuation techniques,\nincluding the discounted cash flow (DCF) model. The inputs to these models are taken from observable markets where\npossible, but where this is not feasible, a degree of judgement is required in establishing fair values. The judgements\ninclude considerations of inputs such as liquidity risk, credit risk and volatility. Any changes in assumptions about these\nfactors could affect the fair value reported in the consolidated financial instruments. For more details on the fair values\nrefer to Note 45.\n31\n185\nKazakhtelecom JSC Consolidated financial statements\nNOTES TO THE CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS (continued)\n4. INVESTMENT IN ASSOCIATES AND JOINT VENTURES (continued)\nAssociates\nAs at 31 December 2022, the Group had a 49% interest in QazCloud LLP, a service company providing IT\ninfrastructure maintenance services. The Group\U2019s interest in QazCloud LLP was accounted for using the equity method\nin the consolidated financial statements. On 20 September 2022, the Board of Directors of Kazakhtelecom JSC decided\nto sell 49% of share of QazCloud LLP through a public tender. On 26 December 2022, the tender winner was selected,\nwith the selling price of KZT 4,590,010 thousand; however, the transaction required the Parent\U2019s approval. Investment\nin QazCloud LLP was classified as assets held for sale from 20 September 2022, and the use of the equity method was\ndiscontinued. On 3 March 2023, Kazakhtelecom JSC received approval of the sale of 49% of share in QazCloud LLP to\nDaneker Sala LLP at a price of KZT 4,544,676 thousand, and the agreement was signed on 20 March 2023. On\n28 March 2023, Kazakhtelecom JSC received the full amount of payment. During 2023, QazCloud LLP paid dividends\nof KZT 50,219 thousand to the Group. The gain on the sale of the share in QazCloud LLP was KZT 876,945 thousand;\nit was recorded within operating income in the consolidated statement of comprehensive income.\n11. IMPAIRMENT TESTING\nGoodwill\nFor impairment testing, goodwill acquired through business combinations was allocated to three cash-generating units\n(\U201cCGUs\U201d) (\U201cIP TV\U201d, \U201cKcell JSC\U201d and \U201cMobile Telecom-Service LLP\U201d).\nIP TV CGU is part of the fixed telecommunications segment, while Kcell JSC and Mobile Telecom-Service LLP are a\npart of the mobile telecommunication segment.\nGoodwill relates to the assembled workforce and synergy from integration of the acquired subsidiaries into the Group.\nThe carrying amount of goodwill allocated to each of CGUs was as follows:\nIn thousands of tenge 2024 2023\nKcell JSC IP TV Mobile Telecom-Service LLP* (Note 41) 96,205,967\n53,489,943 53,489,943\n2,706,335 2,706,335\n56,196,278 152,402,245\n* As at 31 December 2024, goodwill attributable to Mobile Telecom-Service LLP was reclassified to assets held for sale (Note 41).\nThe Group performed its annual impairment test in December 2024 and 2023.\nImpairment test\nPursuant to IAS 36, goodwill and other intangible assets with indefinite useful lives and intangible assets not yet\nbrought into use must be tested for impairment annually or more often if indicators of impairment exist. Other assets are\ntested for impairment when circumstances indicate that there may be a potential impairment.\nFor the purpose of the impairment testing, the Group assessed the recoverable amount of each cash-generating unit to\nwhich goodwill was allocated or where indicators of impairment were identified.\nThe Group determined that the fact that, as at 31 December 2024, the Group\U2019s net assets were higher than the market\ncapitalisation as an indicator of impairment and performed an impairment test. In 2023, in line with the previous years,\nthe impairment test was performed as at 31 December. Since there were impairment indicators, the impairment test for\nthe Group was performed for each separate cash generating unit (CGU). Accordingly, the Group tested its CGU\n\U201cKazakhtelecom JSC\U201d. The impairment test identified that the recoverable amount of non-current assets was higher than\nthe carrying amount of the Group\U2019s assets.\nIn 2024, the recoverable amounts of all cash generating units were determined based on the value-in-use calculation.\nThis valuation technique uses cash flow projections based on the actual operating results and business plans approved\nby management and appropriate discount rates reflecting the time value of money and risks associated with respective\ncash-generating units. For the periods not covered by the management\U2019s business plans, terminal value is used. The\nterminal value is calculated based on the cash flow projections by extrapolating the results of the respective business\nplans using a zero real growth rate.\n40\n188\nKazakhtelecom JSC Consolidated financial statements\nNOTES TO THE CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS (continued)\n11. IMPAIRMENT TESTING (continued)\nImpairment test (continued)\nEstimation of future cash flows requires assumptions to be made in respect to uncertain factors, including management\nexpectations in relation to Earnings before Interest, Taxation, Depreciation and Amortisation (EBITDA) margin, timing\nand amount of capital expenditures, terminal growth rates and appropriate discount rates to reflect the risks involved.\nTherefore, EBITDA margin and capital expenditures used for value-in-use calculation are primarily derived from\ninternal sources, based on past experience and extended to include management expectations. For the purposes of\nimpairment testing, EBITDA is calculated as earnings before interest, taxation, depreciation and amortisation measured\non the basis consistent with IFRS consolidated financial statements.\nThe table below presents EBITDA margin applied for value-in-use calculation of related CGUs:\nIn thousands of tenge 2024 2023\nKcell JSC IP TV 36.78%\U201348.38% 37.3%\U201345.7%\n5%\U201310.8% 2%\U20137%\nKazakhtelecom JSC 25.07% 23.5%\U201324.3%\nThe table below presents capital expenditure as a percentage of revenue applied for value-in-use calculations of related\nCGUs:\nIn thousands of tenge 2024 2023\nKcell JSC IP TV 18.4% 18.0%\n0.0% 1.0%\nKazakhtelecom JSC 13.0 % 10.9%\nThe table below presents terminal growth rates applied for value-in-use calculations of related CGUs:\nIn thousands of tenge 2024 2023\nKcell JSC IP TV 4.10% 3.20%\n0.00% 5.00%\nKazakhtelecom JSC 4.10% 5.00%\nThe table below presents pre-tax rates for the discounting of cash flows in functional currencies of related CGUs:\nIn thousands of tenge 2024 2023\nKcell JSC IP TV 15.24% 13.88%\n15.03% 15.41%\nKazakhtelecom JSC 16.24% 15.41%\nSensitivity to changes in assumptions \U2013 IP TV and Kcell\nReasonably possible changes in EBITDA margin, growth rate beyond the forecast period and discount rates do not lead\nto additional impairment at IP TV and Kcell.\nSensitivity to changes in assumptions \U2013 Kazakhtelecom\nThe calculation of value-in-use for Kazakhtelecom CGU is most sensitive to the following assumptions:\nEBITDA margin included in the financial plan;\nGrowth rate for cash flow extrapolation beyond the forecast period;\nDiscount rate.\nEBITDA margin\nThe decrease in EBITDA margin by 0.5% from 25.07% to 24.57% gradually in the forecast period would result in the\nloss from impairment in Kazakhtelecom CGU of KZT 10,158,897 thousand.\n41\n6. EMPLOYEE BENEFIT OBLIGATIONS\nState contribution plan\nThe Group pays social tax according to the current statutory requirements of the Republic of Kazakhstan. The social tax\nand salary accruals are recorded in expenses as incurred. In addition, the Group withholds 10% and 2% of the salary of\nemployees paid as contributions of employees to the accumulating pension funds and as mandatory social health\ninsurance, respectively. These expenses are recorded in the period when they were incurred.\nEmployee benefit obligations\nAs at 31 December, the total employee benefit obligations of the Group comprised the following:\nIn thousands of tenge 2024 2023\nPresent value of defined benefit pension plan obligations Present value of obligations for other long-term payments 16,358,644 14,959,697\n143,552 147,399\n16,502,196 15,107,096\nA defined benefit pension plan provides for the fulfilment of obligations under the pension provision in accordance with\nthe Collective Agreement concluded between the Company and employees. Other long-term payments include\nanniversaries, funeral payments, and others. ASSET RETIREMENT OBLIGATION\nThe provision for the asset retirement obligation is recorded at the discounted value of expected costs to bring the sites\nand facilities to their original condition using estimated cash flows and is recognised as part of the cost of the specific\nasset. The cash flows are discounted at a current pre-tax rate that reflects the risks specific to the asset retirement\nobligation.\nThe movements in the provision for the asset retirement obligation as at 31 December were as follows:\nIn thousands of tenge 2024 2023\nProvision for asset retirement obligation as at 1 January\n14,535,891 9,542,760\nAccrued provisions (Note 8) 678,707 3,227,077\nUnwinding of discount (Note 39) 432,101 1,847,576\nLiabilities directly associated with assets held for sale (Note 41) (10,633,247)\nUse of the provision (81,522)\nProvision for asset retirement obligation as at 31 December 5,013,452 14,535,891\nCurrent portion (Note 31) 955,785\nNon-current portion 5,013,452 13,580,106\n27. COMPENSATION FOR PROVISION OF UNIVERSAL SERVICES IN RURAL AREAS\nAccording to the approved regulatory documents on subsidisation, losses for the provision of universal\ntelecommunications services in rural areas are subject to subsidies. The amount of compensation is calculated as the\ndifference between the costs and actual revenues from the unprofitable universal telecommunications services.\nThe total amount of compensations received for 2024 amounted to KZT 5,025,725 thousand (2023:\nKZT 8,853,903 thousand).\nAs at 31 December 2024, there are no unfulfilled conditions or contingencies attached to these grants.\n62\n6. DISCONTINUED OPERATIONS\nMobile Telecom-Service LLP\nOn 30 April 2024, the Group\U2019s general meeting of shareholders decided to sell 100% interest in Mobile Telecom-\nService LLP (MTS), a subsidiary, to Power International Holding (PIH), a third party. On 30 April 2024, MTS was\nclassified as a disposal group held for sale and as discontinued operations since MTS represents the Group\U2019s separate\nsignificant line of business providing GSM and LTE mobile telecommunication services.\nOn 4 June 2024, the Group entered into an agreement on the sale of MTS with PIH Interconnect Ltd. (PIH\U2019s\nsubsidiary).\nOn 12 November 2024, amendments were made to the main agreement, according to which the rights and obligations\nunder the agreement were assigned to another subsidiary of PIH - PIH Communication LLC. According to the signed\nagreement, the parties agreed on preliminary conditions that must be met to complete this transaction for the transfer of\nownership and control from Kazakhtelecom JSC to PIH Communication LLC. As of 31 December 2024, the transfer of\nownership of 100% of the stake in MTS was not completed due to the ongoing process to fulfill the conditions for the\ncompletion of the transaction, and, accordingly, the Group retained control over MTS. The sale of 100% interest in\nMTS was completed in January 2025 (Note 47). The selling price of the 100% share in MTC was USD 1,100,000,000,\nwhich includes a component of contingent consideration.\n67\n6. FINANCIAL INSTRUMENTS AND FINANCIAL RISK MANAGEMENT OBJECTIVES AND\nPRINCIPLES\nImpairment losses on financial assets\nImpairment losses on financial assets for the year ended 31 December 2024 comprise accrued/(reversed) allowance for\nexpected credit losses for trade receivables in the amount of KZT 3,672,190 thousand (Note 15), other current financial\nassets in the amount of KZT 75,335 thousand (Note 17), cash and cash equivalents in the amount of KZT (2.396)\nthousand (Note 20) (2023: trade receivables in the amount of KZT 10,516,790 thousand, other current financial assets in\nthe amount of KZT (65.659) thousand, cash and cash equivalents in the amount of KZT (7.247) thousand).\nImpairment losses on non-financial assets\nImpairment losses on non-financial assets for the year ended 31 December 2024, comprise accrued/(reversed)\nallowance for impairment for advances paid for non-current assets for KZT 280,745 thousand (Note 8), advances paid\npaid for current assets for KZT 511,864 thousand (Note 16), and impairment of property and equipment for\nKZT 748,698 thousand (Note 8) (2023: provision for impairment of advances paid for non-current assets for\nKZT (554.636) thousand, advances paid for current assets for KZT 385,726 thousand, and impairment of property and\nequipment for KZT 965,123 thousand and impairment of intangible assets for KZT (35,314) thousand).\nThe Group\U2019s principal financial instruments include loans, lease liabilities, cash and cash equivalents, bank deposits,\nreceivables and payables, assets under reverse repurchase agreements and financial assets at amortised cost. The main\nrisks associated with the Group\U2019s financial instruments include interest rate risk, currency risk and credit risk. In\naddition, the Group monitors market risk and liquidity risk associated with all financial instruments.\nInterest rate risk\nInterest rate risk is the risk that the value of a financial instrument will fluctuate due to changes in market interest rates.\nAs at 31 December 2023, the Group had no loans or borrowings with floating interest rates and was not exposed to the\nrisk of changes in market interest rates. In 2024, the Group issued bonds with a floating interest rate on Astana\nInternational Exchange JSC. The Group\U2019s exposure to the interest rate risk relates primarily to the Group\U2019s bonds with\nthe floating interest rate, which is equal to the average value of base rates of the National Bank of the Republic of\nKazakhstan during the coupon period plus the fixed margin of 0.5%\U20131%.\nThe following table demonstrates the sensitivity to reasonably possible changes in interest rates on that portion of loans\nand borrowings. The Group is exposed to credit risk from its operating activities (primarily trade receivables)\nand from its financing activities, including deposits with banks and financial institutions, foreign exchange transactions\nand other financial instruments.\nTrade and other receivables\nFinancial instruments in which the Group\U2019s credit risk is concentrated are primarily trade and other receivables. The\ncredit risk associated with these assets is limited due to the large number of the Group\U2019s customers and the continuous\nmonitoring procedures for customers and other debtors.\nAn impairment analysis is performed at each reporting date using a provision matrix to measure expected credit losses.\nThe provision rates are based on days past due for groupings of various customer segments that have similar loss\npatterns (i.e., by geographical region, product type, customer type and rating, and coverage by letters of credit or other\nforms of credit insurance). The calculation reflects the probability-weighted outcome, the time value of money and\nreasonable and supportable information that is available at the reporting date about past events, current conditions and\nforecasts of future\neconomic conditions. Generally, trade and other receivables are written-off if past due for more than one year and are\nnot subject to enforcement activity. The maximum exposure to credit risk at the reporting date is the carrying amount of\neach class of financial assets disclosed in Notes 12, 15 and 17.\nFinancial instruments and cash deposits\nIn accordance with the financial policy, the Group places free cash in several of the largest Kazakhstani banks (with the\nhighest credit ratings). To manage the credit risk associated with the placement of free cash in banks, the Group\U2019s\nmanagement periodically conducts procedures for assessing the solvency of banks. To facilitate such an assessment,\ndeposits are primarily placed in banks, where the Group already has comparable credit obligations, a current account\nand can easily monitor the activities of such banks.\n74\nIntegrated Annual Report / 2024\nKazakhtelecom JSC NOTES TO THE CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS (continued)\nConsolidated financial statements\nCash balance Balance on deposit accounts\n2024 2023 2024 2023\n45. To maintain or adjust the capital structure, the\nGroup may adjust the dividend payment to the holders of common shares, return equity to shareholders or issue new\nshares. FINANCIAL INSTRUMENTS AND FINANCIAL RISK MANAGEMENT OBJECTIVES AND\nPRINCIPLES (continued)\nValuation techniques and assumptions\nThe following describes the methodologies and assumptions used to determine the fair values for those financial\ninstruments which are not already recorded at fair value in these financial statements.\nAssets for which their fair value approximates their carrying amount\nFor financial assets and financial liabilities that are liquid or have a short term maturity (less than three months) it is\nassumed that their fair value approximates their carrying amount. This assumption is also applied to demand deposits\nand savings accounts without a specific maturity.\nFinancial liabilities carried at amortised cost\nThe fair value of loans obtained is measured by discounting future cash flows using rates currently existing for\noutstanding amounts with similar terms, credit risk and maturity.\n79\n6. COMMITMENTS AND CONTINGENCIES\nOperating environment\nIn Kazakhstan, economic reforms and the development of the legal, tax and administrative infrastructure that meets the\ndeveloped markets reforms, as well as policy.\nare still in process. The future stability of the Kazakhstan economy will largely depend on these\non the effectiveness of the Government\U2019s actions in the area of economy, financial and monetary\nCapital commitments\nThe Group generally enters into contracts for the completion of construction projects and purchase of\ntelecommunication equipment. As at 31 December 2024, the Group had contractual obligations in the total amount of\nKZT 77,112,435 thousand (VAT included) (31 December 2023: KZT 97,469,118 thousand (VAT included)) mainly\nrelated to the purchase of telecommunication equipment and the construction of the telecommunication network.\nLicense commitments\nUnder the terms of certain licences on the provision of wireless telecom services, the Group has certain obligations in\nterms of the coverage area of its network. The Group is obliged to expand the cellular telecommunication coverage to\nthe regions along the major highways and small-sized towns and urban-type communities of the Republic of\nKazakhstan. The Group\U2019s management believes that the Group is in compliance with the terms of the licences.\nIn December 2022, the Group participated in a radio frequency spectrum public auction for 5G mobile communications.\nThe Group won two lots: 3600\U20133700 MHz and 3700\U2013 3800 MHz. On 22 June 2023, the Group met all conditions of the\nauction and recognised an intangible asset for 5G radio frequencies use for KZT 78,034 million, with the estimated\nuseful life of 15 years. According to the conditions attached to the award of frequencies to the Group, it undertakes to\nactivate 3,527 5G base stations throughout the country, with a specified number of base stations in each region. For\n2024 and 2023, the Group fulfilled its licence obligations and activated 784 and 391 base stations, respectively. The\nGroup committed to activate 784 5G base stations yearly until the end of 2027. During 2024, Mobile Telecom-Service\nLLP and Kcell JSC, the Group\U2019s subsidiaries, signed a network sharing agreement for 5G to meet the licence\nobligations for 5G networks.\nTaxation\nTax legislation and regulatory framework of the Republic of Kazakhstan are subject to constant changes and allow for\ndifferent interpretations. In addition, management believes that international agreements, under which the Group works\nwith non-residents residing in International Telecommunication Union, and which provide for certain tax exemptions,\nhave a priority over national tax legislation. Instances of inconsistent opinions between local, regional and national tax\nauthorities are not unusual. The current regime of penalties and interest related to reported and discovered violations of\nKazakhstan\U2019s tax laws is severe. Penalties are generally 80% of the taxes additionally assessed and interest is assessed\nat the refinancing rate established by the National Bank of Kazakhstan multiplied by 1.25. As a result, penalties and\ninterest can amount to multiples of any assessed taxes. Fiscal periods remain open to review by the authorities in respect\nof taxes for five calendar years preceding the year of review.\nDue to the uncertainty surrounding the tax system in the Republic of Kazakhstan, the ceiling amount of taxes, penalties\nand interest, if any, may exceed the amount expensed at the date and accrued as at 31 December 2024. Management\nbelieves that as at 31 December 2024 its interpretation of the relevant legislation is appropriate and the Group\U2019s tax\npositions will be sustained, except as provided for or otherwise disclosed in these consolidated financial statements.\nState grant related to the frequency fee\nThe Group presented a summary report on expenditures aimed at financing broadband Internet access projects in urban\nand rural areas, including capital and operating costs required to provide broadband Internet access services in urban\nand rural settlements throughout the Republic of Kazakhstan. Management believes that there are no outstanding\nconditions or unforeseen circumstances related to these grants.\n80\n81\n6. COMMITMENTS AND CONTINGENCIES (continued)\nArbitration against Amdocs companies (continued)\nOn 13 September 2023, a Settlement Agreement in the amount USD 6 million (equivalent of\nKZT 2,762,348 thousand) was signed between the Group and Amdocs on voluntary execution of the arbitration\ndecision in order to reduce payments as well as risks associated with the execution of the arbitration award. As at 31 December 2024 and 2023, the\nbalance of the provision is equal to zero.\nAgency for the Protection and Development of Competition\nOrder of the Agency for the Protection and Development of Competition of the Republic of Kazakhstan dated\n15 June 2022\nIn accordance with Order No. 42-OD of the Agency for the Protection and Development of Competition of the Republic\nof Kazakhstan for the city of Almaty (hereinafter referred to as the \U201cAPDC\U201d) dated 15 June 2022 (hereinafter referred to\nas the \U201cOrder\U201d), an investigation was initiated against the Group on the grounds of a violation provided for in Article\n174 (1) of the Entrepreneurial Code of the Republic of Kazakhstan. The initial audited period was the period from\n1 January 2020 to 12 September 2022. The APDC observed a high price for mobile telecommunications services for the\nbrand of Kcell. The subject of investigation is the establishment of factual data confirming or refuting the commission\nof a violation by the Group, expressed in maintaining a monopoly high price to limit or eliminate competition.\nThe Group appealed the resolution on the investigation in the Agency for the Protection and Development of\nCompetition on 26 July 2022; however, the appeal was rejected on 16 August 2022. As a result of the appeal, the\ninvestigation was suspended by APDC on 28 July 2022.\nDuring 2023, the Group filed a notice of appeal against the Order. On 9 November 2023, the Supreme Court of the\nRepublic of Kazakhstan held a hearing. The Court found Order No. 42-\n1 January 2020 to 31 December 2021. The investigation was resumed on 27 November 2023.\nOn 13 December 2023, the Group filed an appeal against the resumption of investigation. On 22 December 2023, the\ninvestigation was suspended due to the filed appeal.\nThe Supreme Court of Kazakhstan upheld the lower courts\U2019 resolutions considering the case as the one that is not\nsubject to administrative legal proceedings, and the cassation appeal was rejected.\nOn 30 January 2025, the Group received the judicial decision on the resumption of the investigation from\n29 January 2025. The Group is preparing the response to the APDC\U2019s inquiry as part of the investigation.\nThe Group\U2019s management assessed the risk of violation of anti-monopoly law as possible, and therefore no provision\nwas accrued to losses potentially arising from any of the above investigations and notifications as at 31 December 2024.\nOrder of the Agency for the Protection and Development of Competition of the Republic of Kazakhstan dated\n21 June 2023\nIn accordance with Order No. 38-OD of the Agency for the Protection and Development of Competition of the Republic\nof Kazakhstan for the city of Almaty dated 21 December 2023, an investigation was initiated against the Group. The\nsubject of the investigation is the prevention of actions in coordination with the competitors to establish and maintain\nprices for telecommunication services in May to July 2023. As part of the investigation, the APDC sent an inquiry to\nthe Group requesting information required for performing an investigation. On 10 January 2024, the Group contested\nthis requirement in the APDC.\nDuring 2024, the Group received dismissals of appeals from the lower-level courts. The Group filed the cassation\nappeal on 16 October 2024. APPENDICES Glossary\n3G (third generation) third-generation mobile communications technology \U2014 a set of services that combine both high-speed mobile access\nwith Internet services and radio communication technology that creates a data channel.\n4G (fourth generation)\na generation of mobile communications with heightened demands. The fourth generation usually includes promising\ntechnologies that make it possible to transfer data at a rate exceeding 100 Mbit/s \U2014 mobile and 1 Gbit/s \U2014 fixed\nusers.\n5G (fifth generation) a high-speed wireless Internet, a fifth-generation technology that provides more efficient communications and\naccess to data and services by increasing the speed of data receipt/transmission and broadening the range\nADSL (Asymmetric Digital\nSubscriber Line)\nan asymmetric digital subscriber line \U2014 modem technology in which the available bandwidth of the channel\nis distributed between the proceeding and entering traffic asymmetrically\n\U0410\U041c\U0422\U0421 automatic long-distance telephone communication\nBroadband or high-speed Internet\naccess\nInternet access at a data rate that is higher than the maximum possible when using dial-up access using a modem\nand a public telephone network\nAPI (Application Programming\nInterface) a description of how one computer programme may interact with another programme\nARPU (Average Revenue Per\nUser) average revenue per month per subscriber\nB2B (Business to Business) a term for commercial relations between legal entities\nB2C (Business to Consumer) a term that refers to a commercial relationship between a legal entity and a consumer\nB2G (Business to Government) a term that refers to commercial relations between a legal entity and the state.\nB2O (Business to Operators) a term that refers to commercial relations between a legal entity and the state\nBig Data big data processing\nBlockchain a continuous sequential chain of blocks containing information, organized according to specific rules. Most often,\ncopies of the chain of blocks are stored on many different computers independently of each other\nCDMA (Code Division Multiple\nAccess)\nmultiple access with code division, digital cellular (wireless) communications network. CDMA is recommended\nby the global organisation for standardisation of communications as the most promising for building third-generation\nnetworks.\nCR cash register\nCSR corporate social responsibility\nDWDM (Dense Wave Division\nMultiplexing)\nthe most reliable technology for the underlying infrastructure of multiservice and mobile networks, ensures a sharp\nincrease in network throughput and provides a wide range of fundamentally new communications services\nEBITDA (Earnings Before\nInterest, Taxes, Depreciation and\nAmortisation)\nthe Company\U2019s profit before deduction of interest on loans, profits tax and depreciatio\nESG factors (Environmental.\nSocial. Governance) environmental, social and management factors\nIntegrated Annual Report / 2024\n204\nFirewall a technology barrier designed to prevent unauthorised or unsolicited communications between computer networks\nor hosts.\nFMC \U2014 One contact (fixed mobile\nconvergence)\na technology barrier designed to prevent unauthorised or unsolicited communications between computer networks\nor hosts.\nFOCL RS fiber-optic communications lines in rural settlements\nFTTH (Fiber to the Home) fiber optic cable to the home (individual/private home)\nFTT\U0445 (fiber to the x) fiber-optic connection technology\nFWA (Fixed Wireless Access) 4G-based wireless internet technology used in areas not covered by fibre optic lines.\nGSM a global standard of digital mobile cellular communications with time and frequency split, is highly secure and\noperates in 2G networks. The main purpose is to make calls and exchange messages\nGPON (Gigabit passive optical\nnetwork) GB passive optical networks\nIaaS (Infrastructure as a Service) infrastructure as a service, for example, applications\nvirtual servers and a virtual network; the client may install any software and\nICT information and communication technologies\nIPTV (Internet Protocol Television) television using Internet protocol, technology (standard) of digital television in data transmission networks using IP\nprotocol, used by digital cable television operators, and the new generation of television\nIP-transit a service to provide managed and high-speed Internet access through modern optical data transmission networks\nusing the BGP protocol. BGP is a protocol of dynamic route between autonomous systems used on the Internet.\nIoT (Internet of Things) a common name for technologies that allow devices built into individual objects to send and receive information via\nthe Internet (wired or wireless)\nLoRa (Long Range) a technology and a method of modulation of the same name\nLTE (Long-Term Evolution) is a wireless high-speed data transmission standard for mobile phones and other data terminals\nNPS (Net Promoter Score) Consumer Commitment Index or Company (Recommendation Readiness Index), used to assess readiness for repeat\npurchases. It is one of the main indices for measuring customer loyalty\nOTT (Over the Top) a method of providing video services over the Internet\nROACE (Return On Average\nCapital Employed) return on average capital employed\nSaaS (Software as a Service) software as a service, for example, e-mail or other office application; the client uses the application, basic\napplication settings are managed by the provider\nSAC (Subscriber Acquisition\nCost) a metric that reflects the Company\U2019s total costs on attracting one buyer\nSAC subsidiary and affiliated company\n6.
